The $32,390,000 City of Cleveland, Ohio, Water Pollution Control Revenue Bonds, Series 2016 (Green Bonds) (the 
“Series 2016 Bonds”) are special obligations of the City of Cleveland, Ohio (the “City”) issued under and secured by the 
provisions of the Trust Agreement between the City and Zions Bank, a Division of ZB, National Association, as trustee 
(the “Trustee”), to provide funds to (i) pay Capital Costs relating to the acquisition, construction and improvement 
of the System, (ii) fund the Debt Service Reserve Requirement for the Series 2016 Bonds, and (iii) pay the costs of 
issuance of the Series 2016 Bonds. See “
Appendix  B - d efinitions  And  s ummAry  of  CertAin  t erms  And  p rovisions  of  the  
t rust  Agreement .” 
The Series 2016 Bonds will be secured under the Trust Agreement, on a parity with any Additional Bonds, by a 
pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the Special Funds (all as defined herein).  See “ s eCurity  And  s ourCes  of  
p Ayment  of  the  Bonds .”
Interest on the Series 2016 Bonds is payable each May 15 and November 15, beginning November 15, 2016.  The 
Series 2016 Bonds will be initially issued as fully registered bonds under a book-entry system, and will be registered 
initially in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee for The Depository Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”).  
Purchases of book-entry interests in the Series 2016 Bonds will be made in denominations of $5,000 and any integral 
multiple thereof.  DTC, or its nominee, will receive all payments with respect to the Series 2016 Bonds from the 
Trustee.  DTC is required by its rules and procedures to remit such payments to participants in DTC for subsequent 
disbursement to the owners of book-entry interests.  Holders of book-entry interests in the Series 2016 Bonds will not 
receive physical delivery of bond certificates.  The Series 2016 Bonds in certificated form as such will not be transferable 
or exchangeable, except for transfer to a nominee of DTC or as otherwise described in this Official Statement.  Principal 
of and redemption premium, if any, and interest on, the Series 2016 Bonds will be paid to Cede & Co. as the registered 
owner.  See “
Appendix  g – B ook -e ntry  o nly  s ystem ” hereto.
The Series 2016 Bonds are subject to optional and mandatory sinking fund redemption prior to maturity as 
described herein. See “d esCription  of  the  s eries  2016 Bonds  – Redemption Provisions.”
The Series 2016 Bonds will be special obligations of the City and will not represent or constitute a 
general obligation, bonded indebtedness or a pledge of the general credit or taxing power of the City, the 
State of Ohio or any political subdivision thereof.  The holders of the Series 2016 Bonds will not have the 
right to have excises or taxes levied by the City, the State of Ohio or the taxing authority of any political 
subdivision thereof for the payment of debt service charges. See “
CertAin  i nvestment  ConsiderAtions  And  r isk  
fACtors  – Limited Obligations.”
The Series 2016 Bonds are offered when, as and if issued by the City and accepted by the Underwriters, subject to 
the opinions on certain legal matters relating to their issuance by Squire Patton Boggs (US) LLP, Bond Counsel, and 
certain other conditions.  Certain legal matters will be passed upon for the City by Barbara A. Langhenry, its Director 
of Law.  Certain legal matters will be passed upon for the Underwriters by their counsel, Calfee, Halter & Griswold LLP.  
It is expected that delivery of the Series 2016 Bonds in definitive form will be made to DTC on or about April 14, 2016.

and there shall not be any sale of, the Series 2016 Bonds by any person in any jurisdiction in 
which it is unlawful to make such offer, solicitation or sale. 
The information and expressions of opinion in  this Official Statement are subject to 
change without notice.  Neither the delivery of  this Official Statement nor any sale made 
hereunder shall create, under any ci rcumstances, or give rise to  any implication that there has 
been no change in the affairs of the City since its date. 
Any statements made in this Official St atement which involve opinions or estimates, 
whether expressly stated to be such, are made as  such and are not representations of fact or 
certainty, and no representation is made that any of those statements have been or will be 
realized.  Information in this Official Statem ent that has been derived by the City from its 
officials and other sources is beli eved to be accurate and reliable.  Information other than that 
obtained from official records of  the City has not been independe ntly confirmed or verified by 
the City, and its accuracy is not guaranteed.

OFFICIAL STATEMENT 
Relating to 
$32,390,000 
CITY OF CLEVELAND, OHIO 
WATER POLLUTION CONTROL REVENUE BONDS 
SERIES 2016 (GREEN BONDS) 
INTRODUCTION 
The City of Cleveland, Ohio (t he “City”) is furnishing this Official Statement, including 
the cover page and appendices, to provide certain information in connection with the issuance 
and sale by the City of its $32,390,000 City of Cleveland, Ohio, Water Pollution Control 
Revenue Bonds, Series 2016 (Green Bonds) (the “Series 2016 Bonds”).  The Series 2016 Bonds 
and any series of Additional Bonds hereafter issued under the Trust Agreement are referred to 
collectively as the “Bonds.”  All capitalized terms used but not otherwise defined in this Official 
Statement shall have the meanings ascribed to them in the Trust Agreement.  See “A
PPENDIX B – 
DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN TERMS AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST AGREEMENT.”  
The Series 2016 Bonds are being issued (i ) to pay Capital Costs relating to the 
acquisition, construction and impr ovement of the System, (ii) fund the Debt Service Reserve 
Requirement for the Series 2016 Bonds, and (iii) to  pay the costs of issu ance of the Series 2016 
Bonds, as described under “Purpose of Issue” herein. 
This introduction is not a summary of this Official Statement.  It is only a brief 
description of and guide to, and is qualified by, more complete and detailed information 
contained in the entire Officia l Statement, including the cove r page and appendices hereto, and 
the documents summarized or described herein.  A full review should be made of the entire 
Official Statement.  The offering of the Series 20 16 Bonds to potential inves tors is made only by 
means of the entire Official Statement. 
Issuer 
The City is a municipal corporation duly orga nized and validly existing under its Charter 
and the Constitution and laws of the State of Ohio (the “State”).  The Division of Water Pollution 
Control (the “Division”) along with the Division of Water, Cleveland Public Power, the Division 
of Fiscal Control, and the Office of Utilitie s General Administration make up the City’s 
Department of Public Utilities. The Division is responsible for cleaning and maintaining the 
network of sewers in the City. The network carries sanitary se wage, combined stormwater and 
sewage, and industrial waste from their points of  origin to sewage processing facilities for 
treatment and disposal.  See “THE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL.”  
Security and Sources of Payment for the Series 2016 Bonds 
The Series 2016 Bonds will be special obligati ons of the City and will not represent or 
constitute a general obligation, bond ed indebtedness or a pledge of  the general cr edit or taxing 
power of the City, the State of Ohio or any po litical subdivision thereof.  The holders of the  
 2 
Series 2016 Bonds will not have the right to have excises or taxes levied by the City, the State of 
Ohio or the taxing authority of any political s ubdivision thereof for the payment of debt service 
charges. See “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS  – Limited 
Obligations.” 
The Series 2016 Bonds are issued and secure d under the Master Trust Agreement, dated 
as of April 14, 2016 (the “Master Trust Agreement”), by and between the City and Zions Bank, a 
Division of ZB, National Association, Clevela nd, Ohio, as trustee (the “Trustee”), as 
supplemented by the First Supplemental Trust Agreement dated as of April 14, 2016, by and 
between the City and the Trustee (the “First Su pplemental Trust Agreement” and together with 
the Master Trust Agreement and as the Master  Trust Agreement may be further amended and 
supplemented from time to time, the “Trust Agreement”).   
Upon issuance and delivery, the Series 2016 Bonds will be secured under the Trust 
Agreement on parity with any Additional Bonds s ubsequently issued.  After the issuance of the 
Series 2016 Bonds, the aggregate outstanding pr incipal amount of Bonds secured by the Trust 
Agreement will be $32,390,000.  See “O UTSTANDING BONDS AND OTHER OBLIGATIONS – 
Outstanding Bonds” and “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS  – 
Additional Bonds.” 
Purpose of Issue 
The City is issuing the Series 2016 Bonds to (a) pay Capital Costs relating to the 
acquisition, construction and improvement of th e System, (b) fund the Debt Service Reserve 
Requirement for the Series 2016 Bonds, and (c) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2016 
Bonds.  The “System” consists of the wastewat er collection and dispos al system owned and 
operated by the City, including all Waste Water Facilities thereof, as extant or as that system 
may be hereafter modified, improved, supplem ented or extended. “Waste Water Facilities” 
consist of facilities for the purpose of treating,  neutralizing, disposing of, stabilizing, cooling, 
segregating, or holding wastewater. “Capital Costs” means the costs of acquisition and 
construction of Waste Water Facilities of the Syst em and all other costs and expense as may be 
necessary or incident thereto. See “A PPENDIX B – DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN 
TERMS AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST AGREEMENT.” 
Green Bond Designation & Green Projects 
The mission of the Division is to provide supe rior leadership, excellent customer service 
and innovative stormwater and wast ewater infrastructure management for a safe and sustainable 
environment. The Division is currently undertak ing a number of capital improvement projects 
relating to the acquisition, construction and operation of Waste Water Facilities designed to fulfill 
its mission. Such facilities include  wastewater collection facilities which meet the discharge 
standards in the National Pollution Discha rge Elimination System (“NPDES”) permit and 
wastewater collection and pumping  facilities which reduce sewage spills. Accordingly, the City 
has designated the capital improvements to be fi nanced with the proceed s of the Series 2016 
Bonds as “Green Projects” based on the enviro nmental benefits of these capital improvements 
and has designated the Series 2016 Bonds, the proceeds of which will be used to pay Capital 
Costs of such capital improvements, as “Green Bonds.”    
 3 
The purpose of labeling the Series 2016 Bonds as  Green Bonds is to allow investors to 
invest in environmentally benefi cial projects. The te rms “Green Project” and “Green Bond” are 
neither defined in nor related to provisions in the Trust Agreement. Owners of the Series 2016 
Bonds do not have any security other than as provided in the Trust Agreement, and owners of the 
Green Bonds do not assume any specific project risk related to any of the projects funded 
thereby. The Green Bonds, as with all other Bonds, are revenue bonds secured by a pledge of and 
lien on the Net Revenues of the System. See “S
ECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF THE 
BONDS.” 
The Green Projects to be funded with the proceeds of the Series 2016 Bonds fall into the 
following two categories:  
• Stormwater Projects: Stream channel restoration, removal of shoaling and woody growth, 
and other restoration, rehabilitation and improvements to the Euclid Creek Flood Control 
project between Lake Eerie and Villaview Ro ad, located on the east side of the City; 
constructing and repairing catch basins and manholes throughout the City.  
• Sewer Projects : Constructing and installing replacement sewers and repairing and 
rehabilitating existing sewers throughout the City as needed; rehabilitating and relining 
sewers at various locations in the City; rehabilitating and repairing sewer service 
connections throughout the City; replacing structurally deteriorated sewer lines at various 
locations throughout the City to  prevent flooding to properti es, basement flooding, street 
flooding, and illicit discharges; acquiring equipment and prof essional services; investing 
in information technology projects. 
For additional information concer ning the Green Projects, see “T
HE DIVISION OF WATER 
POLLUTION CONTROL — Capital Improvement Programs” and “APPENDIX E - Feasibility Report” 
and Appendix B thereto.  
A sub-account will be created within the C onstruction Fund for each Series of Bonds 
issued under the Trust Agreement, including a sub-account for the proceeds of the Series 2016 
Bonds to facilitate tracking the spending of th e proceeds. The net proceeds of the Series 2016 
Bonds will be spent only on the above-described Green Projects. 
The City assumes no obligation to ensure that these projects designated as Green Projects 
comply with any legal or other standards or principles that relate to Green Projects. The City will 
provide annual updates regarding the Green Project s and use of the proceeds of the Green Bonds 
in the form of Appendix F on its website: http://www.clevelandwpc.com. See “A PPENDIX F – 
FORM OF UPDATES REGARDING GREEN PROJECTS AND GREEN BONDS.” The City will provide 
such updates until the City comp letes these projects or until all proceeds of the Series 2016 
Bonds have been spent, at whic h time no further updates will be provided. For the avoidance of 
doubt, such updates related to the Green Projects  are not part of the Continuing Disclosure 
Annual Filing (see “APPENDIX D – FORM OF CONTINUING DISCLOSURE AGREEMENT”).

Description of the Series 2016 Bonds 
Denominations:  The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued  in fully registered form under a 
book-entry only system.  Book-entry interests in the Series 2016 Bonds will be originally 
available for purchase in principal amounts of $5,000 and integral multiples thereof.    
Redemption:  The Series 2016 Bonds maturing on or after November 15, 2026 are 
subject to prior redemption, by an d at the option of the City, in  whole or in part (in whole 
multiples of $5,000), on any date on or after Nove mber 15, 2025, in any order of maturity, at a 
redemption price of 100% of the principal am ount thereof, plus accrued interest to the 
redemption date. Certain of the Series 2016 Bonds  are also subject to mandatory sinking fund 
redemption prior to maturity. See “D ESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2016 BONDS – Redemption 
Provisions.”   
Book-Entry System: The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued under a book-entry only 
system, registered in the name of Cede & Co., as bond owner and nominee for The Depository 
Trust Company (“DTC”), New York, New York, to which payments of prin cipal of, and interest 
and any premium on (“Debt Service”), the Seri es 2016 Bonds will be made.  Purchases and 
transfers of the Series 2016 B onds may be made in book-entry form only; purchasers will not 
receive bond certificates.  See “APPENDIX G – BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.” 
The City and the Trustee will recognize and treat DTC (or any successor securities 
depository) or its nominee as the owner of the Series 2016 Bonds for all purposes, including 
payment of Debt Service, notices and enforcem ent of remedies.  Cred iting of Debt Service 
payments and transmittal of notices and other communications by DTC to Direct Participants 
and Indirect Participants, and by Di rect Participants and Indirect Participants to the beneficial 
owners of the Series 2016 Bonds, are the responsibilities of those persons and will be handled by 
arrangements among them.  The City and the Trustee have no responsibility or liability for any 
aspect of the records or  notices to, or payments made on account of, book-entry ownership, or 
for maintaining, supervising or reviewing any records relating to that ownership.  See “A
PPENDIX 
G – BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.”  
Tax Matters 
In the opinion of Squire Patton Boggs (US)  LLP, Bond Counsel, under existing law (i) 
assuming continuing compliance with certain  covenants and the accuracy of certain 
representations, interest on the Series 2016 Bonds is excluded from gross income for federal 
income tax purposes and is not an item of tax preference for purposes of the federal alternative 
minimum tax imposed on individuals and corporations and (ii) interest on, and any profit made 
on the sale, exchange or other disposition of, th e Series 2016 Bonds, are exempt from all Ohio 
state and local taxation, except the estate tax, the domestic insurance company tax, the dealers in 
intangibles tax, the tax levied on the basis of the to tal equity capital of fi nancial institutions, and 
the net worth base of the corporate franchis e tax. Interest on the Series 2016 Bonds may be 
subject to certain federal taxes imposed only on certain corporations, including the corporate 
alternative minimum tax on a portion of that interest. For a more complete discussion of the tax 
aspects, see “T
AX MATTERS,” “CERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Tax 
Considerations,” and “APPENDIX C - FORM OF BOND COUNSEL OPINION.”

The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued under authority of Article XVIII of the Ohio 
Constitution, the Charter of the City, Ordinan ce No. 29-16 passed by the Council of the City on 
January 25, 2016 (the “General Bond Ordinance”) , Ordinance No. 28-16 passed by the Council 
of the City on January 25, 2016 (t he “Series 2016 Bond Ordinance” ) and a Certificate of Award 
delivered pursuant thereto (the “Certificate of Award,” and t ogether with the General Bond 
Ordinance and the Series 2016 Bond Ordinance,  the “Series 2016 Bond Legislation”).  The 
Series 2016 Bonds will be secured by the Trust Agreement.

SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS 
Sources of Payment 
Under the terms of the Trust Agreement, the Bonds are special obligations payable solely 
from and secured by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the Spec ial Funds, subject to 
bankruptcy laws and other laws affecting creditors’ rights and to  the exercise of judicial 
discretion. See “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS  – Limited 
Obligations” and “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS  – Bankruptcy.” 
The Net Revenues generally consist of the Reve nues derived from the ownership, operation, use 
and services of the System less the Operating E xpenses thereof.  The Special Funds consist of 
the Construction Fund, the Debt Service Fund, the De bt Service Reserve Fund (to the extent that 
a series of Bonds is secured by the Debt Service Reserve Fund), the S ubordinated Debt Service 
Fund, the Rate Stabilization Fund, the Contingency Fund, and the Balance Subfund. See 
“APPENDIX B – DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN TERMS AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST 
AGREEMENT – Pledge of and Lien on Net Revenues and Special Funds; Funds and Subfunds.”  
Any pledge of or lien on any re venues, money or other intangible  property not in the custody of 
the Trustee will be valid and enforceable only to the extent permitted by law. 
The Series 2016 Bonds will be special obligat ions of the City and will not represent 
or constitute a general obligatio n, bonded indebtedness or a pled ge of the general credit or 
taxing power of the City, the State of Ohio or any political subdivision thereof.  The holders 
of the Series 2016 Bonds will not h ave the right to have excises or taxes levied by the City, 
the State of Ohio or the taxing authority of any political subdivision thereof for the 
payment of debt service charges.  See “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK 
FACTORS – Limited Obligations.” 
Rate Covenant 
The City covenants in the Trust Agreement, subject to all applicable requirements and 
restrictions imposed by law, that at all times it will prescribe, charge and collect such rates, 
rentals and other charges for the use of the services of the System and shall restrict the Operating 
Expenses of the System in such a way that Ne t Revenues Available for Debt Service (adjusted 
for purposes of clause (i) as described in the foll owing sentence) in each Fiscal Year shall be not 
less than the greater of (i) 120 % of Debt Service on all Bonds then Outstanding payable during 
that Fiscal Year or (ii) 100% of the sum of: (A) Debt Service on all Bonds th en Outstanding 
payable during that Fiscal Year, (B) all requi red deposits to the Debt Service Reserve Fund 
during that Fiscal Year,  (C) all required depos its to the Subordinated Debt Service Fund and to 
any reserve fund securing Subordi nated Indebtedness during that Fi scal Year, (D) all required 
deposits to the Contingency Fund during that Fiscal Year, and (E ) debt service payable on any 
other obligations payable from the Balance Subf und and deposits to any reserve funds securing 
such other obligations during that Fiscal Year.  For purposes of clause (i) of the preceding 
sentence, but not for the purpose of clause (i i) of the preceding se ntence, “Net Revenues 
Available for Debt Service” for any Fiscal Year  shall include any amount s transferred from the 
Rate Stabilization Fund to the Revenue Fund dur ing such Fiscal Year, but shall be reduced by 
any amounts transferred from the Revenue Fund to  the Rate Stabilization Fund during that 
period. For purposes of determining the City’s compliance with the rate covenant set forth  
 7 
herein, the amount of any Direct Payments received by the City or the Trustee in any Fiscal Year 
shall be credited against (i) Debt Service in such Fiscal Year if such Direct Payment related to 
Bonds or (ii) debt service on S ubordinated Indebtedness in such Fiscal Year if such Direct 
Payment related to Subordinated Indebtedness. Th e City currently is not receiving any Direct 
Payment.  
If in any Fiscal Year the Net Revenues Available for Debt Service shall be less than the 
amount required under the Trust Agreement, the City  shall, within thirty  (30) days following 
receipt by the City of  its audited annual financial statem ent and the written request of the 
Trustee, employ a Consulting Engineer to make r ecommendations within forty-five (45) days as 
to a revision of the rates, fees and charges or Operating Expenses or methods of operation of the 
System, if any, that will result in producing the amount so required in the next succeeding Fiscal 
Year.  The City covenants and agrees, promptly  upon its receipt of such recommendations, to 
revise the rates, fees, and charges or Operating Expenses or methods of operation of the System 
and to take such other action as shall be in c onformity with such recommendations to the extent 
the City feasibly may do so and to notify the Trustee of the actions it has taken.   
Upon the taking by the City of such actions, its failure to comply with the foregoing 
requirements shall not constitute an Event of Default. See “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT 
CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Changes in Market Conditi ons; Conditions of the City; 
Ability to Charge Rates.” 
Debt Service Reserve Fund 
The Trust Agreement establishes a Debt Service Reserve Fund and permits the City to 
establish a Debt Service Reserv e Requirement for each Series of Bonds.  The Trust Agreement 
requires that if on any Interest  Payment Date, the amount in th e subaccount in the Interest 
Subfund or the Principal Subfund for any Series of  Bonds shall be less than the amount required 
to be therein on deposit, the Trustee shall, after deposits are made, if any, into the Subordinated 
Debt Service Fund, the Contingency Fund, the Rate Stabilization Fund, and the Balance 
Subfund, apply the amounts in the a pplicable Subfund, if any, in the Debt Service Reserve Fund 
to the extent necessary to make good any such de ficiency (or the entire amount in the applicable 
Subfund if less than sufficient).  The City may, so long as it will not re sult in a reduction of the 
rating assigned to any of the Bonds, substitute for funds on deposit in th e Debt Service Reserve 
Fund a letter of credit, surety bond  or other credit enhancement f acility issued by a Qualified 
Financial Institution. The City has established a Debt Service Reserve Requirement for the Series 
2016 Bonds.  As a result, deposits will be made to  the Debt Service Reserve Fund for the Series 
2016 Bonds.  
Additional Bonds 
The City may issue Additional Bonds (i.e., additional Series of Bonds payable from Net 
Revenues and secured by the Trust Agreement on parity with the Series 2016 Bonds and any 
other Series of Bonds hereafte r issued) for the purposes of (a) paying Capital Costs or (b) 
refunding, including advance ref unding, for any lawful purpose,  any Outstanding Bonds or 
Subordinated Indebtedness where such refunding w ill not adversely affect the exclusion of the 
interest on any Tax-Exempt Bonds from gross inco me for purposes of federal income taxation.   
 8 
 
Additional Bonds shall be equally  and ratably payable from Net Revenues and shall be secured 
by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and th e Special Funds on a parity with any other 
then Outstanding Bonds (subject to the provisions of the Trust Agreement providing for the 
application thereof).  
For any Series of Additional Bonds that the City issues for the payment of Capital Costs 
or for the purpose of refunding Subordinated I ndebtedness or other obligations other than 
Outstanding Bonds, the City must furnish the Trustee with either (A) a Certificate of the Director 
of Finance certifying that the Net Revenues Availa ble for Debt Service for the preceding Fiscal 
Year or any consecutive twelve (12) calendar months during the eighteen (18)-month period 
immediately preceding the date of original issu ance of the proposed Series of Bonds (in each 
case, the “Test Period”) are in an amount not less than the greater of (1) 120% of maximum 
annual Debt Service on all Bonds then Outstanding and on the proposed Series of Additional 
Bonds or (2) 100% of the sum of: (A) maxi mum annual Debt Servi ce on any Bonds then 
Outstanding and on the proposed Series of Bonds, (B) all required deposits to the Debt Service 
Reserve Fund, (C) all required deposits to the Subordinated Debt Service Fund and to any 
reserve fund securing Subordinated Indebtedness, (D) all required deposits to the Contingency 
Fund, and (E) debt service payabl e on any other obligations paya ble from the Balance Subfund 
and deposits to any reserve funds securing such other obligations, during that Test Period (the 
amounts described in clauses (A) through (E) be ing referred to collectively as the “Test 
Amount”), or (B) a Certificate of the Director of  Finance, which may be, but is not required to 
be, accompanied by or based upon a Certificate of  a Consulting Engineer, certifying that the 
Adjusted Net Revenues for the Test Period are in an amount not less than the greater of (1) 120% 
of maximum annual Debt Service on any Bonds th en Outstanding and on the proposed Series of 
Bonds or (2) 100% of the Test Amount during that Test Period.   
No certification shall be required for any Seri es of Bonds being issued for the purpose of 
refunding Outstanding Bonds, provid ed that the issuance of the refunding Bonds will not result 
in any increase in Debt Service in any Fiscal Year; otherwise, the same certification shall be 
required as for a Series of Bonds for the payment of Capital Costs.  
For purposes of determining the City’s comp liance with the Additional Bonds test set 
forth herein, the amount of any Direct Payment rece ived or expected to be received by the City 
or the Trustee in any Fiscal Year shall be credited  against (i) Debt Service in such Fiscal Year if 
such Direct Payment relates to Bonds or (ii) debt service on Subordinated Indebtedness in such 
Fiscal Year if such Direct Payment re lates to Subordinated Indebtedness. See “C
ERTAIN 
INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Additional Bonds.” The City currently is not 
receiving any Direct Payment. 
Subordinated Indebtedness 
The City may, at any time and from time to time, issue or incur Subordinated 
Indebtedness for the purpose of financing any Capital Costs, pr ovided that such Subordinated 
Indebtedness is secured solely by, and is pa yable solely from, mone ys on deposit in the 
Subordinated Debt Service Fund, or the Balance Subfund, or both. Any Supplemental Trust 
Agreement providing for the issuance of Subordinated Indebtedness shall provide that the trustee 
for such Subordinated Indebtedness shall have no right, power or authority to cause acceleration  
 9 
 
of such Subordinated Indebtedness unless and until the Trustee has exercised its power to 
accelerate the Bonds. See “C ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS  – 
Subordinated Indebtedness.”

(1)  Debt Service Reserve Requirement: as of any date of calculation with respect to any Series of Bonds, as 
specified in the Supplemental Trust Agreement applicable thereto, but subject to the requirements of the 
Master Trust Agreement. 
(2) Contingency Fund Requirement: $1,000,000 or such hi gher amount as the Director of Public Utilities may 
from time to time specify (in writing delivered to the Trustee). Subsequent to any such specification, the 
Director of Public Utilities may re duce the Contingency Fund Requirement from the specified amount, but 
not below $1,000,000.  Upon the issuance of the Series 2016 Bonds, the City will have a balance of 
$1,000,000 in the Contingency Fund funded from cash on hand.  
 11 
 
Revenue Fund.  So long as any of the Bonds remain outstanding, all Revenues of the 
System are required to be deposited in the Revenue Fund, which, pursuant to the Trust 
Agreement, will be held by the City  as a trust fund separate and di stinct from all other funds and 
moneys of the City (except for purposes of i nvestment).  In each month, the amounts in the 
Revenue Fund shall be deposited in the Operati ng Subfund and first applie d to the payment of 
Operating Expenses.  Thereafter, the balance in the Revenue Fund up to the Working Capital 
Reserve shall be deposited in the Working Capital Reserve Subfund and retained as a reserve for 
the payment of Operating Expenses and used for that purpose if the Operating Subfund shall 
have been fully expended. Thereafter, the balance in the Revenue Fund shall be paid at the times 
and in the amounts as follows.  
Debt Service Fund.  To the Debt Service Fund: 
(i) To each subaccount in the Interest  Subfund in the Debt Service Fund, 
monthly and on or before the last day of each month (or such other date as may be 
provided in any Supplemental Trust Agreement), after giving effect to amounts therein on 
deposit, an amount such that, if the same amount were paid in each of the months 
preceding the next Interest Payment Date, the aggregate of the amounts so paid would be 
sufficient to pay the interest  due and payable on that next Interest Payment Date on all 
Outstanding Bonds of the Series to which such subaccount relates; and 
(ii) To each applicable subaccount in the Principal Subfund in the Debt 
Service Fund, monthly and on or before the last  day of each of the twelve months that 
precede a month in which a Serial Maturity Da te occurs or a Sinki ng Fund Installment is 
due (or such other date as may be provided in any Supplemental Trust Agreement), after 
giving effect to amounts therein on deposit, an amount such that, if the same amount were 
so paid in each of the months preceding the ne xt Serial Maturity Date or the next Sinking 
Fund Installment, the aggregate of the amounts so paid would be sufficient to pay the 
principal due on that next Serial Maturity Da te or that next Sinking Fund Installment on 
all Outstanding Bonds of the Series to which such subaccount relates. 
Debt Service Reserve Fund.   To the subaccount established in the Debt Service Reserve 
Fund, monthly and on or before the last day of  each month (or such other date as may be 
provided in any Supplemental Trust Agreement), commencing on the date set forth in the 
applicable Supplemental Bond Ordinance with respect to any Series of Bonds for which the Debt 
Service Reserve Requirement is to be deposited in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, after giving 
effect to any amounts already on deposit therein and pledged to such Series of Additional Bonds, 
an amount such that, if that same amount were  deposited in equal monthly installments, the 
aggregate of the amounts so deposited in such s ubaccount would be equal to the Debt Service 
Reserve Requirement with resp ect to such Series of Additional Bonds on the fifth (5th) 
anniversary of such commencement date.  
Thereafter, if the amount on deposit in such s ubaccount at any time is less than the Debt 
Service Reserve Requirement with respect to such  Series of Additional Bonds, the City shall pay 
to the Trustee for deposit in such subaccount, on or  before the last day of each month following 
the date of such deficiency, an amount equal to  one-twelfth of such deficiency.  The frequency 
and amount of any deposits required shall be s ubject to adjustment pursuant to the Trust  
 12 
 
Agreement so that the deposits re quired into the Debt Service Reserve Fund for any Series of 
Bonds shall be no less frequent than the deposits  required into the Debt Service Fund for the 
principal of and interest on such Bonds. 
Subordinated Debt Service Fund.  To any custodians of th e Subordinated Debt Service 
Fund for deposit therein, such amounts as are re quired to be deposited therein on such dates as 
are specified in the Supplemental Trust Agreemen t or other contracts between the City and the 
holder or holders of the Subordi nated Indebtedness.  If any S upplemental Trust Agreement or 
other contract between the City and the holder or holders of S ubordinated Indebtedness requires 
the establishment and funding a reserve account rela ted to such Subordinated Indebtedness, then 
any required deposits to such reserve account may be made after any deposits otherwise required 
into the Subordinated Debt Service Fund but befo re any deposits required into the Contingency 
Fund and the Rate Stabilization Fund. 
Contingency Fund.  To the Contingency Fund, monthly on or before the last day of each 
month on which the balance in the Contingenc y Fund is less than the Contingency Fund 
Requirement, not less than one-twelfth (1/12) of the amount by which the Contingency Fund 
Requirement exceeds the balance. “Continge ncy Fund Requirement” means $1,000,000 or such 
higher amount as the Dir ector of Public Utilities may from time to time specify (in writing 
delivered to the Trustee) as  the Contingency Fund Requireme nt. Subsequent to any such 
specification, the Director of Public Utilities may reduce th e Contingency Fund Requirement 
from the specified amount, but not belo w $1,000,000. Upon the issuance of the Series 2016 
Bonds, the City will have a balance of $1,000,000 in the Contingency Fund funded from cash on 
hand. 
Rate Stabilization Fund.  To the Rate Stabilization Fund, on any date on which deposits 
are required into the Debt Service Fund, the Debt Service Reserve Fund, the Subordinated Debt 
Service Fund, and the Contingency Fund, and after all such deposits are made, any amounts that 
the City elects to make to the Rate Stabilization Fund. 
Balance Subfund. To the credit of the Balance Subf und, on the first day of each Fiscal 
Year or on the first practicable date thereafter, the City shall deposit any balance remaining in the 
Operating Subfund and the Working Capital Rese rve Subfund in excess of  the Working Capital 
Reserve at the end of the preceding Fiscal Year; provided that the City may at any time provide 
for semiannual or quarterly deposits of such Net Revenues to the Balance Subfund. 
Direct Payments. Upon receipt of any Direct Payment, the City or the Trustee shall cause 
it to be deposited (i) in the appropriate subacc ount in the Debt Servic e Fund if such Direct 
Payment relates to Bonds, and (ii) in the appr opriate account in the Subordinated Debt Service 
Fund if such Direct Payment re lates to Subordinated Indebtedne ss, and shall cause it to be 
applied solely to the purposes to which the Tr ust Agreement permits funds in such subaccount 
and account to be applied. The City currently is not receiving any Direct Payment. 
Rebate Fund. The Trust Agreement establishes the Rebate Fund as a separate deposit 
account (except when invested as therein provide d) in the custody of th e Trustee and requires 
separate accounts to be created in the Rebate Fund for each Series of Bonds that are Tax-Exempt 
Bonds, commencing with the Series 2016 Bonds. The Trust Agreement requires that, at least five  
 13 
 
days prior to the end of the fifth (5th) Bond Y ear and each fifth (5th) Bond Year thereafter for 
each Series of Bonds, including the Series 2016 Bonds, and within five  (5) days after the date on 
which all outstanding Bonds of such Series are paid or deemed paid in full, the City shall 
calculate, or shall furnish information to and engage an independent certified public accounting 
firm to calculate, the Rebate Amou nt as of the end of that Bond Y ear or the date of such final 
payment. Within thirty (30) days  after the end of the fifth (5th ) Bond Year and every fifth (5th) 
Bond Year thereafter, the Trustee, acting on behalf of the City and at the written direction of the 
City, shall pay to the United St ates in accordance with Secti on 148(f) of the Code from the 
moneys then on deposit in the applicable account in the Rebate Fund an amount equal to 90% (or 
such greater percentage not in excess of 100% as the City may di rect the Trustee in writing to 
pay) of the Rebate Amount determined from the date of the original delivery of the Bonds of that 
Series (less the portion of the Rebate Amount, if any, previously paid to the United States).  
Within sixty (60) days after the payment in full of all outstanding Bonds of such Series and upon 
written direction of the City, the Trustee shall pay to the United States in accordance with Section 
148(f) of the Code from the moneys then on deposit in the applicable account in the Rebate Fund 
an amount equal to 100% of the Rebate Amount determined from the da te of the original 
delivery of the Bonds of that Series to the date  of such payment (but less that portion of the 
Rebate Amount, if any, previously paid to the United States) and any moneys remaining in the 
applicable account in the Reba te Fund following such payment sh all be paid to the City.  
Notwithstanding anything to the co ntrary, the moneys needed for any payment required as set 
forth herein may be derived from balances in any of the Special Funds other than the Debt 
Service Fund and the Debt Service Reserve Fund, and the City agrees  to apply those balances to 
that purpose in the followi ng order: the Balance Subfund, th e Rate Stabilization Fund, the 
Contingency Fund, the Subordinated Indebtedness Fund and any related reserve fund or account, 
and the Construction Fund.  
If all the gross proceeds of the Bonds of any Series, with in the meaning of Section 148(f) 
of the Code, are expended for the governmental  purpose for which that Series of Bonds was 
issued within six (6) months of the date of issuan ce of that Series and it is not expected that any 
other gross proceeds of that Seri es of Bonds will arise in the future, then the requirements set 
forth herein apply only to gross proceeds of that  Series of Bonds, if any, that actually do 
subsequently arise.  
Uses of Funds.  No payment needs to be made into a Fund if the moneys in such Fund 
are equal to the required Fund ba lance, if any.  Amounts in the various Funds discussed above 
are required and permitted to be used as follows: 
(i) The Debt Service Fund shall be used only for the payment of Debt Service 
Charges on Bonds and, to the extent provided in the Trust Agreement, for the purchase 
for cancellation or redemption of Bonds. 
(ii) The Debt Service Reserve Fund shal l be used only to make up any 
deficiency in the Debt Service Fund with re spect to Debt Service Charges on Bonds that 
are secured thereby, subject to the require ment that amounts in the Balance Subfund, the 
Rate Stabilization Fund, the Contingency F und, and the Subordinated Debt Service Fund 
be applied to make up such deficiency prio r to drawing from the Debt Service Reserve 
Fund.  
 14 
 
(iii) The Subordinated Debt Service Fund shall be used to make up any 
deficiency in the Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any deficiency in the Debt 
Service Reserve Fund, to the extent necessary, subject to the requirement that amounts in 
the Balance Subfund, the Rate Stabilization Fund, and the Contingency Fund be applied 
to make up such deficiency prior to draw ing from the Subordinated Debt Service Fund. 
The remaining amounts on deposit in the Subordinated Debt Service Fund shall be 
applied to the payment of the principal of and interest and any premium on Subordinated 
Indebtedness as and when due or to the re quired funding of any special reserve account 
established for any Subordinated Indebtedness. 
(iv) The Contingency Fund shall be used to make up any deficiency in the 
Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any defi ciency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, 
to the extent necessary, after first draw ing on the Balance Subfund and the Rate 
Stabilization Fund, and otherwise may be used  by the City for the payment of Capital 
Costs or for the purpose of redeeming Bonds. 
(v) The Rate Stabilization Fund shall be used to make up any deficiency in the 
Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any defi ciency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, 
after first drawing on the Balance Subfund. In addition, the City may from time to time 
transfer amounts on deposit in the Rate Stabilization Fund to the Revenue Fund and cause 
them to be applied as Revenues.  
(vi) The Balance Subfund shall be used to  make up any deficiency in the 
Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any defi ciency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, 
and may be used for any lawful System purpose, including, but not limited to, transfers to 
the Subordinated Debt Service Fund for paymen t of the principal of and interest on any 
Subordinated Indebtedness and the funding or  replenishment of any special reserve 
account established for any Subordinated I ndebtedness, but amounts on deposit in the 
Balance Subfund may not be transferred or credited to the Rate Stabilization Fund. 
(vii) The Rebate Fund is not pledged to th e payment of Bond Service Charges, 
is not one of or part of any of the Speci al Funds, and is free and clear of any lien 
thereunder.  At the written request of the C ity, any moneys held as part of the Rebate 
Fund shall be invested or reinvested by the Trustee in Eligible Investments.

Authorization 
The Series 2016 Bonds are being issued pursu ant to the Constitution and laws of Ohio,

The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued under the Trust Agreement in the aggregate 
principal amount set forth on the cover page here of.  The Series 2016 Bonds will be dated their 
respective dates of delivery, will bear interest fr om that date as descri bed herein, payable semi-
annually on May 15 and November 15 of each year (each, an “Interest Payment Date”), 
commencing November 15, 2016 and will mature Nove mber 15 in the years and in the principal 
amounts set forth on the inside front cover page of this Official Stat ement.  Certain of the Series 
2016 Bonds are subject to redemption prior to maturity.  See “REDEMPTION PROVISIONS.” 
The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued initially  as fully registered bonds without coupons 
and in authorized denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof.  The authorized 
denominations of the Series 2016 Bonds are hereinafter called “Authorized Denominations.” 
The Series 2016 Bonds will be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee of 
DTC, and held in the custody of DTC pursuant to  DTC’s book entry only system.  Purchasers of 
beneficial interests in the Series 2016 Bonds will be made in book-entry form, without 
certificates.

will take the actions necessary to  provide for the issuance of B ond certificates to the Holders of 
the Series 2016 Bonds.  See “A

Book Entry Interests.  See “Appendix G – Book-Entry Only System.”  Each Beneficial

Bonds, the particular Series 2016 Bonds to be purchased will be selected in accordance with the

THE CITY OF CLEVELAND 
Introduction 
The City is a municipal corporation and poli tical subdivision of the State of Ohio (the 
“State”).  It is located on the southern shore of Lake Erie a nd is the county seat of Cuyahoga 
County in northeastern Ohio.  The City was inco rporated as a village in 1814 and became a city 
in 1836.  For a more extensive discussion of the City, see “E CONOMIC AND DEMOGRAPHIC 
INFORMATION CONCERNING THE CITY OF CLEVELAND” in APPENDIX A. 
City Government 
The City operates under and is  governed by the Charter, which was first adopted by the 
voters in 1913 and has been and may be further amended by the voters from time to time.  The 
City is also subject to certain general State laws th at are applicable to all cities in the State.  In 
addition, under Article XVIII, Section 3 of the Ohio Constitution, the City may exercise all 
powers of local self-government and may exercise police powers to  the extent not in conflict 
with applicable general Stat e laws.  The Charter provides for a mayor-council form of 
government. 
Legislative authority is currently vested in a 17-member Ci ty Council (“Council”).  The 
terms of Council members and the Mayor are four years.  All C ouncil members are elected from 
wards.  The current terms of the Mayor and Council members expire on January 1, 2018.  
Council fixes compensation of City officials and employees and enacts ordinances and 
resolutions relating to City services, tax levi es, appropriating and bor rowing money, licensing 
and regulating businesses and trades, and other muni cipal functions.  The presiding officer is the 
President of Council, who is elected by the Council members.  Kevin J. Kelley was elected as 
President of Council for the term beginning January 6, 2014.  The Clerk of Council is appointed 
by Council. 
Pursuant to the City Charter,  City Council is required to re -divide the City into wards 
based on the City’s population. Currently, there are 17 wards in the City.   
The City’s chief executive and administrative officer is the Mayor who is elected by the 
voters for a four-year term.  Frank G . Jackson was re-elected to his third term as Mayor of the 
City on November 5, 2013 and began his current term on January 6, 2014.  Prior to assuming 
office as Mayor, Mr. Jackson served as Pres ident of Council from January 2002 through 
December 2005 and as Ward 5 Council Member since 1989.  The Mayor may veto any 
legislation passed by Council.  A veto may be ove rridden by a two-thirds vote of all members of 
Council. 
The Charter establishes certain administrativ e departments, and Council may establish 
divisions thereof or additional departments.  The Mayor appoints all of the directors of the City’s 
14 departments.  
 24 
 
Financial Matters 
The responsibilities for the City’s major financ ial functions are vested in the Director of 
Finance.  The Director of Finance is respons ible for preparing and implementing the City’s 
current operating budget and capital improvement plan, collecting the City’s revenues, and 
procuring the City’s goods and services and making payments therefor.  The Director of Finance 
is also responsible for maintaining an effective system of internal accounting control which 
includes the maintenance of a centralized accounting system and the supervision of the City’s 
internal audit staff.  Preparation and issuance of the City’s internal and external financial reports 
are supervised by the Director of Finance. 
The Director of Finance for the City is Sharon A. Dumas.  Ms. Dumas served as Assistant 
Director of Finance for Budget and Capital from October 13, 2003 until her appointment as 
Director of Finance on March 29, 2006.  Prior to joining the City of Cleveland Finance 
Department, Ms. Dumas worked as Assistant Dir ector of Community Development for the City.  
Ms. Dumas also served as Finance Director for the City of East Cleveland, Ohio from 1988 to 
1994.  Ms. Dumas holds a Master s of Accounting and Financial Information Systems from 
Cleveland State University and has over 30 years of experience in private and public sector 
accounting. 
James T. Hartley was named an Assistant Finance Director in April 2007 and, in addition, 
has served as acting City Treasurer and now C ity Treasurer since April 2008.  Prior to accepting 
his current positions, Mr. Hartley was the Chief Investment Officer for the Ohio Treasurer of 
State from 1999 until 2007.  As a member of the Treasurer’s senior staff, he was responsible for 
overseeing and directing the Stat e’s investment program, includi ng the State Operating Fund, 
STAR Ohio Local Government Investment Pool, and the State Tobacco Settlement Funds. 
James E. Gentile, CPA, returned to the City  as Controller in Fe bruary 2002.  Prior to 
accepting the position, Mr. Gentile was Deputy Aud itor for the Auditor of State’s Office since 
1995 where he planned and supervised audits of cities, school dist ricts and other local 
government agencies.  From 1991 through 1995, he was employed by the City as an accountant 
and, in his final year, as Acting City Controller. 
Elizabeth C. Hruby has served as the City ’s debt manager since 1996.  She is the 
Assistant Secretary to the Sinking Fund Commission.  She has been employed by the City since 
1982 when she began as a Budget Analyst in th e Office of Budget and Management.  She was 
promoted to Operating Budget Manager in 1987 and was responsible for the development and 
monitoring of the City’s annual operating budget.  From January 7, 2002 until April 1, 2002, Ms. 
Hruby served as interim Director of Finance for the City.   
 25 
 
THE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL 
Overview and History 
The Division is responsible for managing the sanitary sewage and stormwater collection 
system and for overseeing matters relating to th e elimination, control a nd regulation of water 
pollution within City limits. The City derives it s authority to own and operate a water pollution 
control utility from the municipal utility provis ions in Article XVIII, Sections 4, 5, 6 and 12 of 
the Ohio Constitution and Section I of the Charter.  The City is empowered by such provisions to 
establish rates and charges for the services provided by the Division, acquire property, and 
construct facilities to provide sewage and stor mwater collection servic es throughout its Service 
Area and perform other necessary functions to operate and maintain the Division. 
The Division was created for the purpose of supplying sewer services to customers within 
the Cleveland metropolitan area. Embarking with a rudimentary system in the late 1800’s, the 
Division developed as the City itself expanded. Until the early 1970’s, the City operated the 
entire system and managed all as pects of sewage treatment and disposal.  In 1972, a court order 
(the “1972 Court Order”) created the Northeast Ohio Regional Se wer District (“NEORSD”) and 
transferred the operation of all wastewater treatme nt plants and interceptors to the NEORSD in 
December 1973. The City retained responsibility fo r the sewer collector system in the City. The 
Division services a significant portion of the entire Cleveland metropolitan area by managing the 
sanitary sewage and storm wa ter drainage collection system . The sewer collection system 
transfers sanitary and storm sewage from its point of origin to an interceptor sewer or treatment 
plant for processing. The System is comprised of  approximately 1,445 miles of sewer lines with 
attendant catch basins and includes 12 pump/lift sta tions (not including the 3 pump stations that 
will be transferred to NEORSD by May 15, 2016) . The Division is also responsible for the 
cleaning of 43,500 catch basins.  
Service Area 
The Service Area of the Division includes all residential, commercial, governmental, and 
non-profit customers located within  City limits. The Service Area also includes customers that 
are physically located outside City limits but whose water meters are located within City limits.  
Sewer Collection 
The Division has responsibil ity over the sewer collection system within the City. The 
Division is responsible for cleaning and maintaining the network of sewers within the City which  
carries sanitary sewage and indus trial waste (which may require pre-treatment) from their points 
of origin to sewage processing facilities for treatment and disposal by NEORSD. The Division 
maintains, cleans, repairs and improves sewers and their appendages. Protecting the health and 
environment of City residents and visitors is vitally important to the Division.  
The System includes three types of sewers. The most prevalent type is sewer pipes that 
collect and transfer combined sanitary and stor mwater flows. Approximately ninety-two percent 
(92%) of the System is served by combined sewe rs. The System also includes separate sanitary 
and storm sewers, as well as a third category of segmented block pipe wherein separate sanitary 
and storm sewers are encased within the same segmented block pipe.   
 26 
 
Stormwater Management 
In addition to operating and maintaining a se wer collection system, the Division is the 
stormwater manager for the City. The Commissione r of Water Pollution Control serves as the 
City’s stormwater manager. A steering comm ittee consisting of representatives from the 
Division, the Cuyahoga Soil and Water Conservation District, the Department of Public Works, 
the Office of Sustainability, the Department of Law, the Department of Building and Housing, 
the Cleveland City Planning Commission, the Divi sion of Waste Collec tion and Disposal, the 
Office of Capital Projects, and the City Council support the management of the stormwater 
system and compliance with the City’s Small Municipal Separate Storm Sewer System (“MS4”) 
permit.  
Non-point stormwater runoff is rainwater and snowmelt that flows over solid, impervious 
surfaces such as streets, sidewalks and park ing lots. Hard, compact soil also can prevent 
stormwater from infiltrating the ground, which can lead to street flooding and erosion. 
Stormwater runoff can carry debris, chemicals, sediment or other pollutants on the ground into 
sewer catch basins and can flow into local wate rways untreated. This can cause contamination of 
drinking water and compromise recreation areas along Lake Erie, which is Northeast Ohio’s 
main source of drinking water.  
The Division’s responsibilities include overa ll management and reporting on stormwater 
compliance including compliance with the Six Minimum Control Measures specified in the MS4 
permit. Of these six measures, the Division is re sponsible for the first three: Public Education 
and Outreach, Public Involvement  and Participation, and Illicit Connection Detection and 
Elimination. The City’s Department of Building and Housing is responsib le for the fourth and 
fifth minimum control measures : Construction Site Stormwater Runoff Control, and Post 
Construction Stormwater Runoff Control. The City’s Department of Public Works and other 
affected departments are responsible for th e sixth minimum control measure: Pollution 
Prevention and Good Housekeeping. 
The City complies with Environmental Pr otection Agency (“EPA”) requirements to 
maintain its stormwater permit. The City’s Pub lic Involvement and Pub lic Education (“PIPE”) 
program focuses on educating the entire community, but  pays particular atte ntion to its separate 
sewer areas, which have separate sewer pipes for stormwater and wastewater. In those areas, also 
called MS4 areas, runoff is discharged untreated  into local waterways. Those discharges can 
cause water pollution and flooding.  
Public education is an important component of the Division’s authority as the City’s 
stormwater manager. Annually, the Division participates in numerous community events to 
inform residents and others about how their pe rsonal actions related to  stormwater runoff can 
impact water quality and impede the free-flowing capacity of the System. 
The Division promotes the use of low-imp act best management practices (“BMP”) to 
help prevent flooding, protect stream channels and improve water quality. Examples of BMPs 
suitable for residential and commercial properties are green roofs covered with grass and plants 
to absorb rain water, downspouts connected to rain barrels to collect rain water for re-use, rain  
 27 
 
gardens with native plants that absorb large amounts of water, and pe rvious pavements that 
absorb and filter rain water. 
Organizational Structure 
The Department of Public Utilities is compos ed of five divisions, including the Division, 
the Division of Water, Cleveland Public Power, the Division of Fiscal C ontrol, and the Office of 
Utilities General Administration.  Each division is revenue generating except for the Division of 
Fiscal Control, which provides general admini stration, accounting, cash management and other 
financial services to the other four divisions. 
The Division is administered and contro lled by the Commissioner of Water Pollution 
Control, who manages all of the personnel, pr ocurement, budget and overall operations of the 
Division, including the System. Th e Commissioner of Water Pollution Control reports to the 
Director of Public Utilities who reports to  the Mayor and City Administration. The Deputy 
Commissioner of Water Pollution Control assists the Commissioner of Water Pollution Control 
in managing the Division.  
Key Management Personnel 
Director of Public Utilities – Robert L. Davis, as Director of the City of Cleveland 
Department of Public Utilities, is responsible for management and oversight of more than 1700 
employees, a budget of approximately $570 million, and all operations within the Division, the 
Division of Water, Cleveland Public Power, the Division of Fiscal Control, the Office of Utilities 
General Administration, as well  as Cleveland’s public access ch annel, TV20. Before taking the 
position of Director in May 2015, Mr. Davis served the City of Warren, Ohio  as the Director of 
Utility Services. In this role, Mr. Davis was responsible for the operation and maintenance of 
Water, Sewer, Sanitation, and Water Pollution Control. Additionally, Mr. Davis oversaw 
Distribution Collections systems and Customer Service and Billing for each of these divisions. 
Mr. Davis has a strong foundation of both admini strative and hands on experience having risen 
through the ranks throughout his 28-year career as a utility pr ofessional. Mr. Davis holds a Class 
IV Water License and has been a member of the American Water Works Association (“AWWA”) 
for more than 25 years. Mr. Davis is currently the Past Chair of the Ohio Section of AWWA in 
addition to having served 5 years on the Ohio Governing Board. Mr. Davis has also served as 
Chair of the Membership Committee for the Ohio Section and works very closely with the Young 
Professionals, Diversity, Strategic Planning, and Finance and Audit committees. In 2015, Mr. 
Davis was inducted into Warren High School’s Distinguished Alumni Hall of Fame.

the Chief Financial Officer for the Department of Public Utilities sinc e May 2015. Prior to that, 
Mr. Badalamenti was an Assistan t Finance Director for the City from July 2014 to April 2015.  
Previously Mr. Badalamenti was Chief Financial Of ficer for the Department of Public Utilities 
from May 2012 to June 2014.  Mr. Badalamenti was the Manager of Internal  Audit for the City 
from October 1999 to April 2012.  Prior to working for the City, Mr. Badala menti served in the

Employees and Employee Relations    
The Division’s personnel budget for Fiscal Y ear 2016 includes 162 full-time and 4 part-
time positions. Of this amount, 125 full-time and a ll 4 part-time positions are currently filled. 
The City recently reorganized a nd moved 16 financial, public af fairs, geographic information 
system, information technology, and human resour ce positions that were within the Division to 
other divisions within the Depart ment of Public Utilities to c onsolidate responsibilities and 
enhance efficiency and coordination. Although th ese positions were moved out of the Division 
personnel budget, these staff continue to support the Division as needed. In addition, the staffing 
level for the Division’s personnel budget for Fiscal Year 2016 remains the same as the Division’s 
personnel budget for Fiscal Year 2015 at 166. Th e Division is in the process of increasing 
operation, maintenance and engineering staff to meet future needs.  
Each of the full-time and part-time employees of the Division is an employee of the City. 
Approximately eighty-nine percen t (89%) of the Division’s employees belong to one of several 
collective bargaining units represented within the City as listed below. Currently fourteen 
employees, primarily upper-level professionals and administrators, do not belong to unions. The 
contracts with all the collective bargaining units listed below are effective from April 1, 2013 and 
through March 31, 2016. The City is in the process of negotiating new thr ee-year contracts to

replace the expiring contracts. At this time, the Division does not anticipate that the new 
contracts will have any material impact on the Division’s operations or financial projections.

Interactions with NEORSD; Key Permits 
Prior to 1973, the City was responsible for both wastewater collections and wastewater 
treatment. Beginning in Decembe r 1973, the ownership and operati on of all of the wastewater 
treatment plants and interceptors were transferred to NEORSD by the 1972 Court Order. 
The Division’s discharge of flows to the NE ORSD interceptor system for transfer and 
treatment at one of NEORSD’s wastewater tr eatment plants is governed by the City’s 
Community Discharge Permit for sanitary sewers and the City’s Community Combined 
Discharge Permit (collectively, the “Discharge Permits”) for combined stormwater and sewers. 
Neither Discharge Permit has an expiration date; however, the Discharge Permits may be 
modified from time to time as necessary to re flect the changing needs and circumstances of 
NEORSD and the Division. The Division is required to submit a Compliance Report Checklist to 
NEORSD on an annual basis to demonstrate th e Division’s complian ce with the Discharge 
Permits and NEORSD’s BMP guidelines.  
The City consistently maintains compliance with the Discharge Permits’ requirements 
which require implementation of a number of BMPs. Under its Community Discharge Permit for 
sanitary sewers, which represents less than 8% of the collection by the System, a peak flow 
limitation of 14.284 million gallons per day is imposed at the Grayton Road connector. Under its 
Community Combined Discharge Permit for combined sewers, no peak flow limits or 
restrictions are currently imposed. However, NE ORSD has the right to impose future limitations 
if required. No limitations, however, are anticipated to be imposed in the foreseeable future.  
Discharge of separated storm water for the Division is regulated  by the City’s MS4 
permit. A new MS4 permit was issued on September 11, 2014. Only a small portion of the 
System consists of separated stormwater sewers. The majority of the System is combined storm 
and sewer service that is regulated under the City’s Discharge Permits.   
 30

economic base and as economic conditions in and around the City continue to improve.

The Division experienced a slight increase in consumption in 2014. This increase was 
due in part to the Division of Water implementing an Automated Meter Reading (“AMR”) 
system which served to reduce the number of  estimated bills and improve meter reading 
accuracy. This is anticipated to be a one-time increase in response to the improved AMR system.

bill charge.  
Projected Customer Accounts and Consumption 
The Division is conservatively projecting continued decreases in consumption in Fiscal 
Years 2016 through 2020. A 2.2% annual decrease in consumption is  being projected to account 
for potential decreases in customer usage and ot her unknown circumstances. This projection is 
consistent with the Division of Water’s projectio ns for water consumption. The total number of 
customers is projected to remain static. The nu mber of customers is based on buildings with 
metered water service that are connected to the System. As long as a building is connected to the 
System, the customers in the build ing will be billed a fixed char ge regardless of the amount of 
water consumed. The Division does not anticipa te any net disconnection of buildings or 
establishments from the System in the foreseeable future.

Billing and Collection Procedures       
The Division’s customers are billed quarter ly based on their meter size (except the 
homestead rate accounts whose charges are not dependent upon meter size) and metered water 
consumption (with a minimum bill charge). Bills are issued by the City’s Division of Water on 
behalf of the Division. The Division’s charges are found on the same bill for water and waste 
collection. The Division of Water charges the Division its allocable share for provision of the 
billing services based on the Division of Water’s cost and number of bills issued.  
The Division typically anticipates a billing colle ction rate of 90%. This  rate is consistent 
with the Division’s current and historical billing collection rates.  
The Division of Water, as the billing agen t for the Division, anticipates changing from 
quarterly billing to monthly billing in the firs t quarter of Fiscal Year 2017 in response to 
customer requests. While the overall charges from the Division of Wate r are anticipated to 
increase due to increased costs associated with additional printing and postage costs, the charges 
per bill will decrease due to the increase in bi lling frequency. Furthermore, because no increase 
in staffing is anticipated to be required and th e increased postage and printing costs will be 
shared among the Division, the Division of Wate r, and the Division of  Waste Collection and 
Disposal, the net increase in the Division’s share of the cost of billing services is anticipated to 
be minimal over the current quarterly billing costs. This increase in billing costs is projected to 
be incurred in Fiscal Year 2017.  
 33 
 
Sewer Rates 
The Trust Agreement provides that the City must charge sewer rates and so restrict 
Operating Expenses as will result in Net Revenues Available for Debt Service in each Fiscal Year 
being not less than 120% of Debt Service on a ll Bonds then Outstanding payable during that 
Fiscal Year.  See “S ECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS – Rate Covenant” and  
“APPENDIX B – DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN TERMS AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST 
AGREEMENT.”  
The Division is responsible for establishing sewer rates and other fees and charges for its 
customers which must be approved by City Council. Th e rates must be at sufficient levels to pay 
for operating and maintenance costs of the System  and debt service on outstanding debt and to 
provide for appropriate contingencies and reserves.  
Sewer rates provide funding for the Division to conduct daily maintenance and repairs to 
the System, including its pump stations. The tabl e below presents the new sewer rates that went 
into effect on April 1, 2015. These rates includ ed both fixed charges and consumption charges. 
Effective April 1, 2015, City Council  approved a new fixed fee ch arge based upon meter size in 
accordance with Ordinance No. 1030-14. The fixe d fee will raise about $39 million over five 
years to address sewer issues more proactivel y and better serve City residents and business 
owners. The last time the City had a sewer rate  increase was in 2006. Under the new sewer fixed 
charges, City residential properties are assessed $12 on their curren t quarterly payment, and that 
fee will increase by $3.00 per quarter in 2017 and in 2019. Properties with larger meters will be 
assessed at a higher rate. In a ddition, the fixed charges are not tied to water consumption, 
resulting in more predictability of charges to be collected. Se wer consumption charges are based 
on water consumption at each property locat ion. See “REVENUES, EXPENSES AND DEBT 
SERVICE - General.”

The Division has a special homestead rate  for homesteads that are single family 
residential property owned and occupied by a person sixty-five (65) years of age or older, or 
homesteads that are single fam ily residential prop erty owned and occupied by a person 
permanently and totally disabled, whose total annual income does not exceed the applicable 
limit, which is $32,500 for 2016. 
The Division has also instituted an affordabili ty program to provide assistance to eligible 
low-income customers. The program offers a reduction of 40%, regardless of the meter size, 
from each quarterly sewer bill for residential customers who have been qualified to receive 
assistance through the federally funded Home Energy Assistance Program (“HEAP”). It is 
anticipated that the resulting reduction in sewer services sales revenue for the Division because 
of the homestead rate will be insignificant. 
Maintenance Practices 
The Division maintains a sewer system preventative maintenance program that includes 
implementation of BMPs, including a comprehensive Capacity Management, Operation, and 
Maintenance (“CMOM”) program. Historically, the maintenance program focused first on 
addressing any complaints and known problem  areas and second on conducting preventative 
maintenance. While these priorities remain, th e Division is increasing  both its preventative 
maintenance efforts and resources and rate of re placement of sewers which are past their useful 
life. The Division has developed a comprehens ive CMOM program to increase preventative 
maintenance investment and reduce the potential of  sanitary sewer overflows (“SSOs”) in a cost 
effective manner. The program includes the following components: Management Plan, Operation 
and Maintenance Plan, Capacity Plan, Overflow Response Plan, Condition Assessment Plan, 
Communications Plan, and Audit Plan. Key elements of the program include:   
 35 
 
• Using a computerized maintenance and mana gement system to track all activities 
including inspections, cleaning, and rehabilitation and replacement projects.  
• Continually updating and maintaining Divisi on sewer maps in Graphic Information 
Systems.  
• Conducting condition assessments to budget a nd plan for upcoming rehabilitation and 
replacement programs.  
• Maintaining adequate inventory of equipm ent and spare parts to allow immediate 
responses to emergencies and prevent SSOs.  
• Developing Standard Operating Procedures.  
• Establishing performance measures and goals.  
• Expanding safety training for employees.  
• Establishing operation and maintenance programs for cleaning and inspections.  
Capital Improvement Programs 
The Division historically employed a pa y-as-you-go capital improvement plan, 
supplemented with grants and low cost loans fr om the OPWC and OWDA for eligible projects. 
The Division’s past plans focused primarily on projects to address street and basement flooding, 
to acquire equipment, and to implement inform ation technology systems. For more information 
on the Division’s past capital improvement projects, see “A PPENDIX E - Feasibility Report - 6.1 
Past Capital Improvements.” 
The Division plans to use approximately $35 million of the proceed s of the Series 2016 
Bonds to fund the majority of its capital impr ovement program for the next three years (2016-
2018), supplemented with cash funding of vehi cles, equipment, and technology projects. For 
more information on the projects to be funded with proceeds of the Series 2016 Bonds, see 
“APPENDIX E - Feasibility Report - 6.2 Projects to be Funded with Series 2016 Bonds” and 
Appendix B thereto. 
In addition to the projects anticipated to be funded with proceeds of the Series 2016 
Bonds, the Division anticipates funding equipment purchases a nd technology investments with 
cash on hand and issuing additional Bonds as needed to fund future capital improvement 
projects. The capital improvement program over the five-year period from 2016 through 2020 
includes project commitments of approximately $64 million. The principal focus of this five-year 
capital improvement program is sewer repair and replacement to rehabilitate and repair aging 
sewer pipes. For more information on the Divisi on’s future capital impr ovement projects, see 
“APPENDIX E - Feasibility Report - 6.3 Future Capital Improvements” and Appendix B thereto.

REVENUES, EXPENSES AND DEBT SERVICE 
General 
The Revenues of the System in clude revenues derived from user consumption charges, 
fixed meter charges, and other miscellaneous revenue.  
User Consumption Charges : Historically, the Division relie d solely on user charges that 
were based on each customer’s billable metered wa ter consumption. The Division still relies on 
such consumption charges, but in Fiscal Year 2015 the Division also implemented a fixed charge 
component based on meter size. For the consump tion charge component, customers are charged 
the same rate per thousand cubic feet (“MCF”) of consumption as metered by the City’s Division 
of Water. The only exception is that certain cu stomers pay a discounted homestead rate if they 
are eligible and have been a pproved based on established ec onomic and social criteria. The 
homestead rate provides customers with a discounted rate which is approximately 40% lower 
than the regular rate to maintain affordability of such rates. The consumption charge also 
includes a minimum bill charge based on a minimum consumption of one MCF per quarter. 
When the Division moves to monthly billing, the minimum charge per bill will be prorated to 
adjust for monthly as opposed to quarterly billing.  
Fixed Meter Charges: Beginning in Fiscal Year 2015, for customers with a water meter, 
the Division instituted a new fixed charge co mponent that varies based on the size of the 
customer’s incoming water meter service. The fi xed charge is in addition to the consumption 
charge and was instituted to address the infrastructure of the System. The fixed charge is 
assessed even if the customer ha d zero water consumption. Similar to the consumption charge, a 
40% discounted homestead fixed ch arge rate is available for qualifying customers to maintain 
affordability of the rates. When the Division moves to monthly billing, which is anticipated to be 
in 2017, the Fixed Meter Charge per bill will be prorated to ad just for monthly as opposed to 
quarterly billing. 
Other Revenue: Other revenue includes interest in come, licenses and permit fee revenue, 
reimbursements/credits from the City, and other miscellaneous revenue. Other revenue represents 
a very small percentage of the Division’s total revenues.

Management Discussion of Results of Operations   
The comparative statement of revenues and expenses for Fiscal Years 2011-2014 set forth 
below has been derived from the financial statements of the Division. The comparative statement 
of revenues and expenses for Fiscal Year 2015 set forth below is based on unaudited figures from 
the Division. The Division is considered an enterprise fund because the operations of the 
Division are similar to a privat e sector business enterprise. A ccordingly, in accounting for the  
 39 
 
activities of the Division, the economic resources measurement focus and the accrual basis of 
accounting are used.  
Fiscal Year 2011 
Operating revenues in 2011 ($22,199,000) decreased by $2,911,000 (11.6%) from 2010 
($25,110,000), mainly due to a decrease in consumption.  
Total operating expenses in 201 1 decreased by $1,042,000 (4.4%) to $22,884,000 
compared to $23,926,000 in 2010.  The components of  the decrease in ope rating expenses in 
2011 were a decrease in operation costs of $683,000, a decrease in maintenance costs of $92,000, 
and a decrease in depreciation expense of $267,000.  
The Division incurred an operating loss  after depreciation of $685,000 in 2011; the 
Division used cash on hand to fund the operating loss. 
Fiscal Year 2012 
Operating revenues in 2012 ($22,876,000) increased by $677,000 (3%) from 2011 
($22,199,000), mainly due to an increase in consumption.  
Total operating expenses in 2012 increased by $1,493,000 (6.5%) to $24,377,000 
compared to $22,884,000 in 2011.  There was an increase in operation costs of $879,000. The 
major component was accrued bad debt expense, which increased by $1,061,000.  
The Division incurred an operating loss after depreciation of $1,501,000 in 2012; the 
Division used cash on hand to fund the operating loss. 
Fiscal Year 2013 
Operating revenues in 2013 ($22,549,000) decreased by $327,000 (1.4%) compared to 
2012 ($22,876,000), mainly due to a decrease in consumption.  
Total operating expenses in 2013  ($22,544,000) decreased by $1,833,000 (7.5%) 
compared to $24,377,000 in 2012.  There was a decrease in operation costs of $962,000. The 
major component of the decrease was accrued bad debt expense, which decreased by $1,945,000. 
In addition, maintenance costs decreased by $984,000. The major components were transfers of 
wages and benefits to capital and maintenan ce utility systems, which decreased by $374,000 and 
$309,000, respectively. The transfer of wages and be nefits to capital wa s calculated using the 
Safe Harbor Rate Method, which decreased overhead costs and increased capital project costs.  
Fiscal Year 2014 
Operating revenues in 2014 ($22,547,000) remain ed approximately the same as in 2013 
($22,549,000), as the 2014 consumption was stable in comparison to 2013.  
Total operating expenses in 2014 increased by $2,164,000 (9.6%) to $24,708,000 
compared to $22,544,000 in 2013.  The major components of the $2,164,000 increase in  
 40 
 
operating expenses in 2014 were increases in  bad debt expense of $1,744,000 and depreciation 
expense of $358,000, offset by a decrease in charges in the Division of Water of $462,000.  
The Division incurred an operating loss after depreciation of $2,161,000 in 2014; the 
Division used cash on hand to fund the operating loss. 
Fiscal Year 2015 
Operating revenues in 2015 ($28,744,000) in creased by $6,197,000 (27.5%) compared to 
2014 ($22,547,000), mainly due to the implementation of  the fixed fee as part of the quarterly 
charged which was in effect for three quarters in 2015. 
Total operating expenses in 2015 ($24,688,000) remained approximately the same as in 
2014 ($24,708,000).
