powers as such Authorized Disclosure Representative. 
“Beneficial Owner” means any person that (a) has the power, directly or indirectly, to 
vote or consent with respect to, or to dispose of ownership of, any Series 2016 Bonds (including 
persons holding Series 2016 Bonds through nominees , depositories or other intermediaries), or 
(b) is treated as the owner of any Series 2016 Bonds for federal income tax purposes. 
“Business Day” means any day other than a Saturday, a Sunday or a day on which the 
offices of the City are closed. 
“Filing Date” means the last day of the ninth month following the end of the Fiscal Year 
(or the next succeeding Business Day if such day is not a Business Day), commencing 
September 30, 2016. 
 “Fiscal Year” means the 12-month period begi nning on January 1 of each year or such 
other 12-month period as the Division shall adopt as its fiscal year. 
“Holder” means, with respect to the Seri es 2016 Bonds, the person in whose name a 
Bond is registered in accordance with the Trust Agreement. 
“MSRB” means the Municipal Securities Rulemaking Board. 
“Obligated Person” means, any person, includi ng the issuer of muni cipal securities (such 
as the Series 2016 Bonds), who is generally co mmitted by contract or other arrangement to 
support payment of all or part of the obligations  on the municipal securities being sold in an 
offering document (such as the Official Statement); the City is the only Obligated Person for the 
Series 2016 Bonds. 
“Official Statement” means the Official Statement for the Series 2016 Bonds dated 
March 31, 2016.  
 D-3 
 
“Specified Events” means any of the events wi th respect to the Series 2016 Bonds as set 
forth in Section 5(a). 
“State” means the State of Ohio. 
“Trust Agreement” means the Master Trust Ag reement, effective as of April 14, 2016, as 
supplemented by the First Supplemental Trust Agreement dated as of April 14, 2016, by and 
between the City and the Trustee. 
Section 3.  Provision of Annual Information. 
(a) The City shall provide (or cau se to be provided) not later than the Filing Date to 
the MSRB and to the Trustee an Annual Filing, wh ich is consistent with the requirements of 
Section 4.  The Annual Filing sh all be submitted in an electr onic format and contain such 
identifying information as is prescribed by the MSRB, and may be submitted as a single 
document or as separate documents comprising a package, and may cross-reference other 
information as provided in Section 4; provided that the Audited Financial Statements of the 
Division may be submitted separately from the ba lance of the Annual Filing and later than the 
Filing Date if they are not available by that date.  If the City’s Fiscal Year changes, it shall give 
notice of such change in the same manner as for a Specified Event under Section 5. 
(b) If the City is unable to provide to th e MSRB an Annual Filing by the Filing Date, 
the City shall, in a timely manner, send a notice to the MSRB in an electronic format as 
prescribed by the MSRB. 
Section 4.  Content of Annual Filing.  The City’s Annual Filing shall contain or include 
by reference the following: 
(a) Financial information and operating data of the type included in the Official 
Statement under the following:  (1) the ta bles under the captions  “OUTSTANDING BONDS 
AND OTHER OBLIGATIONS” and “DEBT SERVIC E SCHEDULE;” (2) the table under the 
subcaption “THE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL – Customer Base;” (3) the 
table under the subcaption “THE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL – Historical 
Customer Accounts and Consum ption;” (4) the table under the subcaption “THE WATER 
POLLUTION CONTROL – Projected Customer A ccounts and Consumption;” (5) the table 
under the subcaption “THE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL – Largest 
Customers of the Division;” (6) the table under the subcap tion “THE DIVISION OF WATER 
POLLUTION CONTROL – Capital Improvement Pr ograms;” and (7) the table “Summary of 
Historical Revenues, Expenses and Debt Service” under the subcaption “REVENUES, 
EXPENSES AND DEBT SERVICE - Historical Revenues and Expenses.” 
(b) The Audited Financial Statements. 
The foregoing shall not obligate the City to pr epare or update projections of any financial 
information or operating data.  If any amendm ent of this Agreement is made concerning the 
operating data or financial information contained in the Annual Filing, the City shall include the 
information required by Section 6 of this Agreement.  
 D-4 
 
Any or all of the items listed above may be included by specific reference to other 
documents, including a comprehensive annual in formational report of the City or official 
statements of debt issues of the City or relate d public entities, which have been submitted to the 
MSRB or the SEC.  The City shall clearly iden tify each such other document so included by 
reference. 
(c) If the Trustee has not recei ved the Annual Filing for a Fi scal Year by its close of 
business on the fifteenth Business Day preceding the Filing Date for that Fiscal Year, the Trustee 
shall provide a notice to the Authorized Disclosure Representative, not later than its close of 
business on the next Business Day, substantially in the form of the attached Exhibit 1, by 
facsimile transmission (or other means similarly pr ompt).  If the Trustee has not received that 
Annual Filing by its close of business on the Filing Date, the Trustee shall provide a notice to the 
Authorized Disclosure Representa tive, not later than its close of  business on the next Business 
Day, substantially in the form of the attached  Exhibit 2, by facsimile transmission (or other 
means similarly prompt).  The City shall be entitled to provide to the Trustee written evidence of 
the submission of the Annual Filing in accordan ce with Section 3 above, including a certificate 
of the Authorized Disclosure Repr esentative as to the relevant facts, and, if applicable, a written 
statement regarding any failure to comply with S ection 3 above.  The Trustee shall be entitled to 
rely conclusively upon any written evidence provid ed by the City regarding the provision of that 
information to the MSRB.  If, in any instance, the required information was not timely filed or 
the City fails to provide evidence by 3:00 p.m., Cleveland, Ohio time, on the second Business 
Day following the Filing Date of its timely filing with the MSRB, the Trustee shall send or cause 
to be sent promptly after receipt of any such evidence or statement from the City, but in any 
event not later than its close of business on the third Business Day following the Filing Date, a 
notice substantially in the form of the attached E xhibit 3, modified to refl ect the pertinent facts, 
to the MSRB in an electronic format as prescribed by the MSRB. 
Section 5.  Reporting Specified Events. 
(a) The City shall provide (or cause to be provided) to the MSRB, in an electronic 
format and containing such identifying information as is prescribed by the MSRB and in a timely 
manner but not later than ten Business Days after th e occurrence of the event, and to the Trustee, 
notice of any of the following events with resp ect to the Series 2016 Bonds, as specified by the 
Rule: 
(1) Principal and interest payment delinquencies; 
(2) Non-payment related defaults, if material; 
(3) Unscheduled draws on debt servic e reserves reflecting financial 
difficulties; 
(4) Unscheduled draws on credit enhancements reflecting financial 
difficulties;  
(5) Substitution of credit or liquidity providers, or their failure to perform; 
(a)  
 D-5 
 
(6) (Issuance of) Adverse tax opinions,  th e issuance by the Internal Revenue 
Service of proposed or final determinations of taxability, Notices of 
Proposed Issue (IRS Form 5701-TEB) or other material notices or 
determinations with respect to the tax status of the security ( i.e., the Series 
2016 Bonds), or other material events  affecting the ta x status of the 
security; 
(7) Modifications to rights of security holders, if material; 
(8) Bond calls, if material, and tender offers; (b) 
(9) Defeasances; 
(10) Release, substitution, or sale of property securing repayment of the 
securities, if material; (c) 
(11) Rating changes; 
(12) Bankruptcy, insolvency, receivership or similar event of the Obligated 
Person;  Note:  For the purposes of the event identified in this 
subparagraph, the event is considered to occur when any of the following 
occur: the appointment of a receiver, fi scal agent or similar officer for an 
Obligated Person in a proceeding under the U.S. Bankruptcy Code or in 
any other proceeding under state or federal law in which a court or 
governmental authority has assumed juri sdiction over substantially all of 
the assets or business of the Obligated  Person, or if such jurisdiction has 
been assumed by leaving the existing governmental body and officials or 
officers in possession but subject to th e supervision and orders of a court 
or governmental authority, or the entr y of an order confirming a plan of 
reorganization, arrangement or liqui dation by a court or governmental 
authority having supervision or jurisd iction over substantially all of the 
assets or business of the Obligated Person. 
(13) The consummation of a merger, conso lidation, or acquisition involving an 
Obligated Person or the sale of all or substantially all of the assets of the 
Obligated Person, other than in the ordi nary course of business, the entry 
into a definitive agreement to undertak e such an action or the termination 
of a definitive agreement relating to any such actions, other than pursuant 
to its terms, if material; and 
(14) Appointment of a successor or additional trustee or the change of name of 
a trustee, if material.

Section 6.  Amendments.  The City reserves the right to amend this Agreement, and 
noncompliance with any provision of this Agreem ent may be waived, as may be necessary or 
appropriate to (a) achieve its compliance with a ny applicable federal secu rities law or rule, (b) 
cure any ambiguity, inconsistency or formal def ect or omission and (c) address any change in 
circumstances arising from a change in legal re quirements, change in law or change in the 
identity, nature or status of the City or t ype of business conducted by the City.  Any such 
amendment or waiver shall not be effective unl ess the Agreement (as amended or taking into 
account such waiver) would have materially complied with the re quirements of the Rule at the 
time of the primary offering of the Series 2016 Bonds, after taking  into account any applicable 
amendments to or official interpretations of th e Rule, as well as any change in circumstances, 
and until the City shall have received either (i) a written opinion of bond counsel or other 
qualified independent special counsel selected by the City that the amendment or waiver would 
not materially impair the interests of the Holders or Beneficial Owners or (ii) the written consent 
to the amendment or waiver of the Holders of at  least a majority of th e principal amount of the 
Series 2016 Bonds then outstanding.  An Annual Filing containing any revised operating data or 
financial information shall explain, in narrativ e form, the reasons for any such amendment or 
waiver and the impact of the change on the type of operating data or financial information being 
provided.  If the amendment relates to the accoun ting principles to be followed in preparing 
Audited Financial Statements, (A) the City sha ll provide notice of such change in the same 
manner as for a Specified Event under Section 5 a nd (B) the Annual Filing for the year in which 
the change is made should pres ent a comparison (in narrative fo rm and also, if feasible, in 
quantitative form) between the financial statements or information as prepared on the basis of the 
new accounting principles and those prepared on the basis of the former accounting principles. 
Section 7.  Additional Information.  Nothing in this Agreement shall be deemed to 
prevent the City from disseminating any other in formation, using the means of dissemination set 
forth in this Agreement or providing any other means of communication, or including any other 
information in any Annual Filing or providing notice of the occurrence of an event, in addition to 
that which is required by this Agreement.  If th e City chooses to include any information in any 
document or notice of occurrence of an event in addition to that which is specifically required by  
 D-7 
 
this Agreement, the City sh all have no obligati on under this Agreem ent to update such 
information or include it in any future Annual Filing or notice of occurrence of a Specified 
Event. 
Section 8.  Remedy for Breach .  This Agreement shall be solely for the benefit of the 
Holders and Beneficial Owners from time to time of the Series 2016 Bonds.  The exclusive 
remedy for any breach of the Agreement by the City  shall be limited, to the extent permitted by 
law, to a right of the Holders and Beneficial Owner s to institute and maintain, or to cause to be 
instituted and maintained, such proceedings as ma y be authorized at law or in equity to obtain 
the specific performance by the City of its obligations under this Agreement in a court in 
Cuyahoga County, Ohio.  Any such proceedings shall be instituted and maintained only in 
accordance with Section 133.25(B)(4)(b) or (C)(1 ) of the Revised C ode (or any like or 
comparable successor provisions); provided that any Holder or Be neficial Owner may exercise 
individually any such right to require the City to  specifically perform its obligation to provide or 
cause to be provided a pertinent filing if such a filing is due and has not been made.  The Trustee 
may exercise any such right if requested to do so by the Holders of at least 25% in aggregate 
principal amount of the Series 2016 Bonds then  outstanding, subject to the same conditions, 
limitations and procedures that would apply under the Trust Agreement if the breach were an 
“Event of Default” under the Trust Agreement.  Any Beneficial Owner seeking to require the 
City to comply with this Agreement shall first provide at least 30 days’ prior written notice to the 
City of the City’s failure, giving reasonable de tail of such failure, following which notice the 
City shall have 30 days to comply.  A defau lt under this Agreement shall not be deemed an 
“Event of Default” under the Trus t Agreement, and the sole remedy under this Agreement in the 
event of any failure of the City to comply with  this Agreement shall be an action to compel 
performance.  No person or entity shall be en titled to recover monetary damages under this 
Agreement. 
Section 9.  Performance by the Trustee; Compensation.   
(a) Solely for the purpose of (i) defining the standards of care and performance 
applicable to the Trustee in the performance of its obligations under this  Agreement, (ii) the 
manner of execution by the Trustee of those oblig ations, (iii) defining the manner in which, and 
the conditions under which, the Trustee may be require d to take any action at the direction of the 
Holders, including the condition that indemnificati on be provided, and (iv) matters of removal, 
resignation and succession of the Tr ustee under this Agreement, the Trust Agreement is hereby 
made applicable to this Agreement as if this Agreement were contained in the Trust Agreement; 
provided that the Trustee shall have only such duties under this Agreement as are specifically set 
forth in this Agreement. 
(b) Subject to Section 10 of this  Agreement, the City agrees to pay to the Trustee 
from time to time reasonable compensation for services provided by the Trustee under this 
Agreement and to pay or reimburse to the Tr ustee upon request all r easonable out-of-pocket 
expenses, disbursements and advances incurred or  made by the Trustee in accordance with this 
Agreement and with prior notice to the City, ex cept to the extent that any such expense, 
disbursement or advance is due to the negligence or bad faith of the Trustee.  
 D-8 
 
(c) The obligations of the City under this Section 9 shall survive resignation or 
removal of the Trustee and termination of ot her provisions of this Agreement pursuant to 
Section 11 below. 
(d) The Trustee is a party to this Agreement for and on behalf of the Holders and 
Beneficial Owners of the Series 2016 Bonds and sh all not be considered to  be the agent of the 
City when performing any actions required to be taken by the Trustee under this Agreement. 
(e) The Trustee shall not have any obligation under this Agreement to investigate or 
determine whether any filing made under this Ag reement complies with federal securities laws 
or rules. 
Section 10.  Appropriation.  The performance by the City of its obligations under this 
Agreement shall be subject to the availability of funds and their annual appropriation to meet 
costs that the City would be required to incu r to perform those obligations.  The City shall 
provide notice to the MSRB in th e same manner as for a Specified  Event under Section 5 of the 
failure to appropriate funds to meet costs to perform the obligations under this Agreement. 
Section 11.  Termination.  The obligations of the C ity under this Agreement shall 
remain in effect only for such period that th e Series 2016 Bonds are outstanding in accordance 
with their terms and the City remains an Obligat ed Person with respect to the Series 2016 Bonds 
within the meaning of the Rule.  The obligati on of the City to provide the information and 
notices of the events described above shall term inate, if and when the City no longer remains 
such an Obligated Person.  If any person, othe r than the City, becomes an Obligated Person 
relating to the Series 2 016 Bonds, the City shall us e its best efforts to require such Obligated 
Person to comply with all provisions of the Rule applicable to such Obligated Person. 
Section 12.  Dissemination Agent.  The City may, from time to time, appoint or engage 
a dissemination agent to assist it in carrying out  its obligations under this Agreement, and may 
discharge any such agent, with or without appointing a successor dissemination agent. 
Section 13.  Beneficiaries.  This Agreement shall inure solely to the benefit of the City, 
any dissemination agent, the Participating Underw riter and Holders and Beneficial Owners from 
time to time of the Series 2016 Bonds, and shall create no rights in any other person or entity. 
Section 14.  Recordkeeping.  The City shall maintain r ecords of all Annual Filings and 
notices of Specified Events and other events including the content of such disclosure, the names 
of the entities with whom such disclosures were filed and the date of filing such disclosure. 
Section 15.  Governing Law .  This Agreement shall be g overned by the laws of the 
State.

1      INTRODUCTION AND PURPOSE 
1.1 Introduction and Purpose 
Arcadis U.S., Inc. (Arcadis), has been retained by the City of Cleveland, Ohio (City) and its Division of 
Water Pollution Control (WPC) to provide Consulting Services to prepare a Bond Feasibility Report 
(Report) for the planned issuance of Series 2016 Water Pollution Control Revenue Bonds.  The proceeds 
of the bonds will be used to fund capital improvements to WPC’s wastewater collection system (System). 
WPC’s System includes sanitary sewers, combined sanitary and storm sewers, separated storm sewers, 
wastewater pump stations and related appurtenances and equipment to collect and transfer wastewater 
and stormwater flow.  The System does not include the regulator weirs (structures on sewer systems that 
permit the discharge of excess flow into a relief sewer and the design dry weather flow to continue up to 
its intended outlet) or wastewater treatment facilities. All wastewater collected by the System is conveyed 
to the Northeast Ohio Regional Sewer District (NEORSD) facilities for further transportation and 
treatment.      
The Report includes:  
• A description and condition summary of the System. 
• An overview of WPC's organization and management. 
• A summary of the status of current and proposed capital projects and improvements. 
• A review of regulatory compliance. 
• A summary of historical and projected customer statistics. 
• A review of current and projected financial information. 
• Conclusions regarding the technical, organizational and financial aspects of WPC. 
The technical and financial data reviewed in preparing this Report include existing records and 
documents provided by WPC. The Report summarizes the work completed up to the date of the issuance 
of the Report. Changed conditions occurring or becoming known after such date could affect the material 
presented and the conclusions reached herein to the extent of such changes.  
Arcadis has not independently verified the accuracy of the information provided by WPC and others ; 
however, our Report is based upon the supposition that such sources are reliable and the information 
obtained therefrom is appropriate for the analysis undertaken and the conclusions reached herein.  To the 
extent that the information provided to Arcadis by WPC and others is not accurate or not fulsome to all 
relevant details, the conclusions and recommendations contained in this Report may vary , and are 
subject to change. In addition, the scope of Arcadis’ review did not include any pending or threatened 
litigation that may impact WPC.  The City has stated that there is no significant litigation that it believes 
would have any material impact on WPC’s operations, and as such, Arcadis has prepared its Report 
accordingly and under the presumption of the accuracy of such statement.

2      ORGANIZATION AND MANAGEMENT 
2.1 Division of Water Pollution Control  
WPC is a division of the City’s Department of Public Utilities that provides retail wastewater and 
stormwater collection services to customers in the City. WPC was established by the City on June 21, 
1965, by Ordinance 1599-65. WPC was created for the purpose of supplying sewer services to customers 
within the Cleveland metropolitan area. Beginning with a rudimentary system in the late 1800s, the 
Cleveland sewer system developed as the City itself expanded. Until the early 1970s,  the City operated 
the entire system and managed all aspects of sewage treatment and disposal. 
In 1972, in response to a lawsuit brought on by several communities in Cuyahoga County, a court order 
created the Northeast Ohio Regional Sewer District (NEORSD). The ownership and operation of all 
wastewater treatment plants, interceptors, sewer regulator systems and devices, weirs, retaining basins, 
and some storm water handling facilities were transferred to NEORSD in December 1973. The City, 
however, retained responsibility for the local sewer collection system within the City limits of Cleveland. 
Over the years, various clarifications and agreements have modified the ownership responsibility of the 
City and NEORSD with respect to the assets located within the City’s boundaries. The WPC System in 
2016 includes approximately 1,445 miles of sewers, 121 pump stations, and related appurtenances.   
In accordance with its governing legislation, WPC operates, maintains and manages the System on 
behalf of the City, pursuant to the requirements of the City’s Community Discharge Permits (both the 
Community Combined Discharge Permit and Community Discharge Permit).  The System  transfers 
collected wastewater from its point of collection to a NEORSD interceptor sewer or treatment plant for 
processing. WPC is also charged with municipal regulation of the City’s local stormwater system and as 
such, also regulates matters related to the pollution of watercourses. 
. 
2.2 Organization Structure  
An overview of the current organization structure of WPC is shown on Figure 2-1.  WPC is one of five (5) 
Divisions within the Department of Public Utilities of the City, which also includes Water, Fiscal Control, 
Utilities Administration and Cleveland Public Power.  WPC is managed by the Commissioner of WPC, 
pursuant to the Charter and ordinances of the City, and under the direction of the Director of Public 
Utilities.  
The WPC Commissioner reports to the Director of Public Utilities, who is appointed by and reports to the 
Mayor. The Board of Control, consisting of the Mayor and directors of several departments , establishes 
the rate and charges for WPC, subject to City Council approval. City Council is  the final governing body 
for approval of rates and charges and other matters related to WPC.   Several other City divisions both 
within and outside of the Department of Public Utilities also provide support services to WPC , including,

Section 2.6.

WPC’s 2016 personnel budget includes 162 full-time and 4 part-time positions. Of these, 125 full time and 
4 part-time positions are currently filled. The City recently reorganized and moved 16 financial, public 
affairs, geographic information systems (GIS), information technology (IT), and human resource type 
positions that were within WPC to other divisions within Public Utilities to consolidate responsibilities and 
enhance efficiency and coordination throughout the department. Although these positions were moved 
out of WPC’s personnel budget into other Department of Public Utility’s divisions, these staff continue to 
support WPC as required. In addition, the approved staffing level for WPC’s FY2016 personnel budget 
remains the same as in FY2015 at 166, and WPC is in the process of hiring additional operation, 
maintenance and engineering staff to meet future needs. 
All of the full-time and part-time employees of WPC are employees of the City, and approximately eighty-
nine percent (89%) belong to one of several collective bargaining units represented within the City. There 
are currently 14 employees that do not belong to unions. They include primarily upper level professionals 
and administrators. All of the union contracts are effective from April 1, 2013, through March 31, 2016. 
The City is in the process of negotiating new three-year union contracts to replace the expiring contracts. 
At this time, WPC does not anticipate that the new contracts will have any material impact on WPC’s 
operations or financial projections.   
The organizational structure of WPC generally is consistent with that of wastewater utilities in many large 
cities. The proposed staffing plan adequately addresses all of the core functions of WPC, with certain key 
support services provided by other City divisions. WPC is in the process of expanding its in-house staff 
and capabilities to meet future needs.  
WPC does have on-call professional services and other contracts in place to provide emergency and 
other required services as may be needed to supplement current staff availability and experience. 
2.3 Management Staff 
The WPC Commissioner is responsible for all technical and administrative operations of WPC , and the 
implementation of programs, policies and procedures at the direction of the Director of Public Utilities and 
the Mayor. Mr. Rachid Zoghaib, P.E., currently serves as the Commissioner of WPC, and has served in 
this position since April 2011. Prior to this, Mr. Zoghaib served as Deputy Commissioner for seven (7) 
years and Director of Engineering for almost ten (10) years. Mr. Robert L. Davis is the Director of Public 
Utilities, and began serving in this position in 2015. Mrs. Ramona Lowery is a new Deputy Commissioner 
for WPC, and reports to the Commissioner. Although Mrs. Lowery started in this position in 2015, she is a 
former employee of the City and NEORSD.  WPC is in process of hiring a second deputy commissioner to 
assist in managing the anticipated increase in workload associated with WPC’s plans , and anticipates 
that this position will be filled before the end of the year. Mr. Frank Badalamenti, Chief Financial Officer 
(CFO) of the Department of Public Utilities, is responsible for the financial management of WPC.  
Biographies of key management and operational staff are provided below.

2.4 Interactions with the City 
WPC is a division within the Department of Public Utilities of the City. The City also maintains several 
other departments and divisions that provide key administrative and support services to WPC. The costs 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 2-5  
of these interdepartmental services are charged back to WPC, as WPC operations are financed primarily 
through direct charges to the users of its services. Several of these other divisions, such as the Division 
of Water, also function as separate utilities. WPC’s allocable share of support services costs from these 
departments and divisions is based on the cost of the services provided. The interdepartmental services 
provided to WPC include but are not limited to the following:  
• Billing and collection services; 
• Procurement, accounts payable, and payroll services; 
• Budget, capital improvement planning and bond issuance support; 
• Technology Management Services (IT) and GIS support;  
• Human Resources support for hiring, terminations, and retirements; 
• Legal support for agreements by WPC and claims for and against  WPC;  
• Utilities administration; 
• Motor vehicle maintenance; and 
• Street construction maintenance and repair. 
In FY2013 and FY2014, WPC paid the City approximately $3.5 million and $3.7 million, respectively, in 
interdepartmental charges, of which $2.5 million and $2.4 million were charges from Division of Water for 
billing and collection services. In FY2015, the interdepartmental charges were $5.2 million, of which $3.9 
million was for billing and collection services. The large increase in Division of Water charges for FY2015 
was primarily the result of a one-time payment adjustment by the Division of Water to WPC. Increases 
also were associated with implementation of a new automated meter (AMR) reading program, which 
should serve to increase revenues through elimination of estimated bills and improved reading accuracy. 
Although the Division of Water charges are anticipated to decrease to $3.15 million in FY2016, the WPC 
budget will maintain an estimated $5.1 million in interdepartmental charges for FY2016 to account for the 
additional charges associated with utilities administration and fiscal control. These additional charges 
result from WPC’s prorated share of costs associated with transferred public affairs, GIS, IT, finance and 
related staff from WPC to other divisions within Public Utilities as discussed in Section 2.2.  
Several City divisions retain independent stormwater responsibilities that are coordinated by WPC. For 
example, the City Department of Building and Housing has the responsibility for construction and post -
construction stormwater runoff control and the City Department of Public Works is responsible for 
stormwater housekeeping.  
2.5 Overview of Service Contracts and Agreements 
WPC performs almost all of the management and operation services required for the System using in-
house staff and resources either directly through WPC, or via City support services from other divisions. 
There are several Memorandums of Understanding (collectively, MOUs), on-call service contracts and 
interactions with other agencies that support the delivery of services. These include, but are not limited to:  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 2-6  
• MO Us with the Cuyahoga County Soil and Water Conservation District and the Doan Brook 
Watershed Partners regarding provision of public education for stormwater control.  
• On-call emergency services contracts with various private vendors to assist in conducting 
emergency repairs beyond the in-house resources of WPC. 
• Professional services contracts to provide general engineering services to WPC. These services 
include wastewater system design and planning, sewer system design, regulatory support , bidding 
and construction services, surveying, field representation and operations support.  
Although not governed by contract, WPC also coordinates the delivery of its services with the 
requirements of NEORSD; both as a condition of the City’s discharge permits and as the host community 
for a significant portion of NEORSD’s assets as discussed further below. 
2.6 NEORSD Interactions  
Prior to 1973, the City was responsible for both wastewater collection and wastewater treatment. 
Beginning in December 1973, the ownership and operation of all of the wastewater treatment plants , 
interceptors, sewer regulator systems and devices, weirs, retaining basins, and some stormwater facilities  
were transferred to NEORSD pursuant to a 1972 Court Order. Subsequently, further clarification of the 
maintenance responsibilities of NEORSD-related collection system assets located within the City limits, 
was confirmed by an Agreed Judgment Entry and Court Order (City of Cleveland v NEORSD, Cuyahoga 
County Court of Common Pleas, Case #455021) dated April 2005.  This order specified that these assets 
should be maintained by NEORSD as part of its interceptor system and not maintained by the City.  An 
MOU and Exhibits A-C that are attached to the Agreed Judgment Entry and Appendix D, Figure D-1 
attached to this Report, provides maps and a description of the assets owned and maintained by each of 
the parties under the 2005 Agreed Judgment Entry and the Court Orders. The clarifications included 
confirmation, among other items, that the regulator weirs are the responsibility of NEORSD.  
Updates to the allocation of responsibilities are conducted as needed by mutual agreement between 
WPC and NEORSD. Most recently, this included the transfer of the Mary Street, West 11th Street and 
Stones Levee pump stations from WPC to NEORSD by May 15, 2016.  NEORSD and WPC are also in 
the process of finalizing a stormwater agreement in year 2016, which, under the authority of Title V of 
NEORSD’s Stormwater Management Code, will transfer the operation and maintenance of the assets that 
are part of the Regional Stormwater System, including two of WPC’s detention basins, from WPC to 
NEORSD. These transfers of responsibility are consistent with NEORSD’s Project Clean Lake Long Term 
Control Plan (LTCP), as required by USEPA, and Regional Stormwater Management Program (RSMP) 
goals.  These transfers are by prior mutual agreement between WPC and NEORSD because NEORSD 
has identified these assets as key components for NEORSD’s systems. Upon the transfer, these assets 
will not be considered part of the System, and were not included in the condition assessment review 
conducted by Arcadis as part of the preparation of this Report.  
WPC discharge of flows to NEORSD’s interceptor system for transfer and treatment at NEORSD’s 
wastewater treatment plants is governed by the Community Combined Discharge Permit with NEORSD 
(dated March 1995) for combined sewers (NEORSD Title IV code) and the Community Discharge Permit 
with NEORSD (dated June 1986) for sanitary sewer (NEORSD Title III code). Neither permit has an 
expiration date; however, the permits may be modified if necessary to reflect the changing needs and 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 2-7  
circumstances of NEORSD and WPC. In addition, there are several levels of coordination between WPC 
and NEORSD as summarized below: 
• Monthly NEORSD engineering coordination meetings with WPC engineering participation. 
• Quarterly NEORSD Water Action Committee meetings with WPC representation and 
participation. 
• NEORSD Project Clean Lake LTCP Implementation and Coordination with City on green 
infrastructure projects, problem area studies and flow monitoring. 
• City representation as voting members on NEORSD governing board; of the 7 members of 
NEORSD governing board, 3 are appointed by the City. 
• NEORSD inclusion in the approval process and requirements for any new development and 
redevelopment within the City. 
WPC consistently complies with its Community Discharge Permit and Community Combined Discharge 
Permit (collectively referred to as the Community Discharge Permits) , requirements that require 
implementation of a number of best management practices. Under the Community Discharge Permit for 
the sanitary sewer system, a peak flow limitation of 14.284 million gallons per day (MGDs) is imposed at 
the Grayton Road connector. WPC and NEORSD have not reported any exceedance of this limitation. 
With respect to the Community Combined Discharge Permit, there are no peak flow limits or restrictions 
imposed at this time. NEORSD, however, has the right to impose future limitations, if required. No 
limitations are anticipated to be imposed within the forecast period as (a) the quantity of wastewater flow 
currently delivered to NEORSD is less today than it was when the discharge permit s were issued, (b) the 
System is essentially fully developed, and (c) the City maintains a policy of managing the amount of 
wastewater flow discharged to its collection system to result in peak flow rates at, or less than, what the 
System was designed for. In addition, as part of its LTCP required by USEPA consistent with a consent 
decree, NEORSD is undertaking several improvements for handling wet weather flows, including 
designing a tunnel for capture and storage of peak wastewater flows.   
In addition to wastewater treatment responsibility, NEORSD also supports the WPC stormwater 
management program. On September 15, 2015, the Ohio Supreme Court ruled that NEORSD was 
authorized to implement its RSMP and had authority to charge stormwater fees to fund it.  Under the 
RSMP, NEORSD will collect stormwater management fees from its customers, using the City as its billing 
agent, and use this money as authorized by Ohio Revised Code (ORC) Chapter 6119 for the use, 
services or benefits of a water-resource project afforded to property owners in its defined regional 
stormwater area, including in the City. That includes NEORSD assuming responsibility for millions of 
dollars of necessary maintenance along streams across the region. It is unknown when NEORSD will 
begin assessing the RSMP charges, but collection is anticipated by the end of FY16. Pursuant to 
NEORSD’s RSMP’s Community Cost Share policy, member communities are eligible to receive funding 
for qualifying community-specific stormwater projects pursuant to an application process. A minimum of 
twenty-five percent (25%) of the total annual stormwater fee revenue collected in each member 
community is allocated to the Community Cost-Share Account for each member community. The City is in 
regular communication with NEORSD regarding the RSMP and cost share opportunities.  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 2-8  
3      SYSTEM DESCRIPTION 
3.1 Service Area 
The City is located in northeastern part of the State of Ohio on the southern shore of Lake Erie; 
approximately sixty (60) miles west of the Pennsylvania border. The City is the county seat of Cuyahoga 
County, which is the most populous county in the State of Ohio. The City itself is the second largest city in 
the State of Ohio, covering a land surface area of 77.6 square miles. It is geographically located near the 
mouth of the Cuyahoga River, and extends along the southern shore of Lake Erie. Founded in 1796, the 
City is a diverse city of approximately 390,000 people.   
WPC’s service area includes all areas within the City limits and represents a significant portion of the 
entire metropolitan area tributary to NEORSD interceptor and treatment plants. The service area includes 
residential, commercial, industrial, government and non-profit customers located with the City limits. It 
also includes customers that may be physically outside the City limits, but have their water meters located 
within the City limits. A map of WPC’s service area and the types of sewer service provided within the 
service area is shown in Appendix D. 
3.2 Description of Major Assets 
WPC is responsible for operating and maintaining its wastewater and stormwater collection systems. The 
System currently includes 122 pump stations, over 1,445 miles of both sanitary and stormwater collection 
systems, mostly in the form of a combined sewer collection system, 36,000 manholes, 43,500 catch 
basins, and related equipment as discussed further below. 
3.2.1 WPC Sewer Collection System 
WPC’s System includes three (3) types of sewers.  The most prevalent type are sewer pipes that collect 
and transfer combined sanitary and storm flows. The System also includes separate sanitary and storm 
sewers, and a third category of segmented block pipes wherein separate sanitary and storm sewers are 
encased within the same segmented block pipe. Appendix D, Figure D-2 provides a map that illustrates 
the areas within the City served by combined and separated (including segmented block) sewers. As 
illustrated in Appendix D, Figure D-2, the majority of the System is served by combined sewers.  
Ninety percent (90%) of the sewers have an equivalent pipe diameter of less than sixty (60) inches; with 
the most common pipe size being twelve (12) inches in diameter. The most common type of construction 
(forty-nine percent (49%)) is vitrified clay pipe (VCP), but with significant quantities of both brick (twenty-
eight percent (28%)) and reinforced concrete pipe (eighteen percent (18%)).  The segmented block pipe 
accounts for approximately 42,000 linear feet or less than one percent (1%) of the total linear feet of pipe. 
The majority of the System was constructed in the 1920s, and is estimated to have an average age of 
2 WPC was originally responsible for 15 pump stations. However, 3 will be transferred to NEORSD by May 15, 2016 as discussed in 
Section 2.6. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 3-1 
                                                       
approximately eighty (80) years. Portions of the System, however, date back to the 1870s. Figure 3-1 
presents a graphical summary of WPC’s collection system by age and type.  
 
Figure 3-1.  WPC Sewer Pipe Age and Type 
 
The estimated useful life of a typical sewer is approximately one hundred (100) years, and approximately 
twenty-seven percent (27%) of WPC’s collection system is over one hundred (100) years old. WPC has 
developed a Capacity, Management, Operation, and Maintenance (CMOM) Plan and a comprehensive 
capital program, which includes conducting a Sewer System Evaluation Survey (SSES) to address this 
aging infrastructure. The CMOM is discussed further in Section 4.3 of this Report.  
WPC is responsible for the operation and maintenance of the System within the City limits, including up to 
one (1) foot from the curb line of the roadway. The laterals and connections from the building to one (1) 
foot from the curb line are the responsibility of the building owners. The interceptors and regulators that 
transfer flow from the WPC collection system to NEORSD treatment facilities are the responsibility of 
NEORSD, as described in Section 2, and are therefore not included as WPC assets.  
3.2.2 Stormwater System 
The City’s stormwater system consists primarily of approximately forty-three thousand five hundred 
(43,500) catch basins, which lead primarily to the combined sewer collection system and approximately 
two hundred six (206) miles of separated storm sewers. A significant portion of these separated storm 
sewers are within a segmented block pipe installed in the 1920s. Separate storm and separate sanitary 
flows are channelled within their respective open channel pipe, both enclosed within the same casing. 
Any storm sewer flows in excess of the pipe’s capacity will overflow into the sanitary system.   
The City’s stormwater system is operated and maintained pursuant to its Ohio Environmental Protection 
Agency, National Pollution Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) permit (NPDES No. OHQ000003)  for 
Small Municipal Separate Storm Sewer Systems (Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit). The remainder of the 
City’s stormwater is managed as part of its wastewater collection system as approximately ninety two 
percent (92%) of the WPC’s System is a combined sanitary and storm sewer system.  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 3-2  
The WPC Commissioner serves as the City’s Stormwater Manager for implementing and coordinating the 
best management practices required as part of a stormwater management plan required under its Ohio 
EPA NPDES MS4 permit. A Stormwater Steering Committee consisting of representatives from WPC, 
Cuyahoga County Soil and Water Conservation District, the City’s Departments of Public Works, Law, 
and Building and Housing, Cleveland City Planning Commission, Office of Sustainability, Division of 
Waste Collection, Office of Capital Projects, and City Council implement the stormwater management 
plan across multiple departments for compliance with the City’s Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit. 
WPC’s responsibilities include overall implementation, management, enforcement and reporting on 
stormwater compliance including compliance with the Six Minimum Control Measures as specified in the 
City’s Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit. Table 3-1 summarizes the allocation of responsibility for each of 
these Six Minimum Control Measures.

NEORSD’s RSMP, described in Section 2.6, is anticipated to start shortly and will serve to further

3.2.3 Sewage Pump Stations 
WPC operates and maintains twelve (12) sewage pump stations, which are utilized to transport sanitary 
wastes where gravity is not a viable transport option. This number of pump stations does  not include the 
three (3) pump stations that are transferring from WPC to NEORSD by May 15, 2016 as discussed in

4      OPERATIONS AND MAINTENANCE 
4.1 Sewer Legislation 
Legal authority for WPC’s System derives from the City’s Charter and codes and ordinances, which are 
reviewed and revised as needed. All ordinances are available on the City’s website. WPC’s key sewer 
ordinances are: City of Cleveland Code of Ordinances, Part 5 – Municipal Utilities and Services Code, 
Title VII – Sewers and Sewage Disposal, Chapter 541- Sewer Connections and Sewer Use Code ; 
Charter reference § 163.  
This statutory framework regulates the use of public and private sewers and drains in the City Right-of-
Way. It also requires, among other things, that individual property owners maintain their sewer service 
connections from one foot beyond the curb to the property to be drained and control unacceptable 
discharges to the collection system, including natural watercourses. If a blockage is in the main sewer or 
between the main sewer and a point one foot beyond the existing or proposed curb line of the roadway, 
repairs shall be made by WPC. If the blockage is between the building and one (1) foot beyond the 
existing or proposed curb line of the roadway, WPC advises the owner to engage a licensed and bonded 
sewer contractor to make the necessary repairs.  
WPC also complies with its obligations under its Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit and NEORSD’s Code of 
Regulations, Title III “Separate Sanitary Sewer Code” and Title IV “Combined Sewer Code” and 
associated Community Combined Sewer Discharge Permit and Community Discharge Permit.  
4.2 Sewer Extensions and Connections 
The System is fully developed.  Should new connections to the existing collection system or 
redevelopment projects by developers be proposed, approval by WPC, Cleveland City Planning 
Commission and the Department of Building and Housing, as well as NEORSD will be required. In 
addition, pursuant to City policy, the connections must maintain compliance with WPC’s policy of 
managing the amount of wastewater flow discharged to its collection system as previously discussed in 
Section 2.6. 
4.3 Operation and Maintenance 
WPC maintains a sewer system preventative maintenance program that includes implementation of best 
management practices. Historically, WPC’s program focused first on addressing any complaints and 
known problem areas and second on conducting preventative maintenance. While these priorities remain, 
WPC is increasing both its preventative maintenance efforts and resources and rate of replacement of 
sewers which are past their useful life. WPC has developed a comprehensive draft CMOM plan to 
increase preventative maintenance investment and reduce potential for sanitary sewer overflows (SSOs) 
in a cost-effective manner. Key elements of the program include: 
• Using a computerized maintenance and management system (CMMS) to track all activities 
including inspections, cleaning, and rehabilitation and replacement projects.   
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 4-1  
• Continual updating and maintaining of WPC sewer maps in GIS. 
• Conducting condition assessments in order to budget and plan for upcoming rehabilitation and 
replacement programs.  
• Maintaining an adequate inventory of equipment and spare parts to allow immediate response to 
emergencies and prevent sanitary sewer overflows.  
• Developing Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs). 
• Establishing performance measures and goals. 
• Expanding safety and training for employees. 
• Establishing operation and maintenance programs for cleaning and inspections. 
Currently, the cleaning of the sewers is done by means of a priority schedule in which blocked main 
sewers are completed first. Known problem areas that do not present an immediate concern are then 
prioritized based on available information and scheduled for cleaning. As work load permits, preventative 
maintenance cleaning is then performed. The goal of WPC is to increase preventative maintenance 
cleaning so that all mains are cleaned, at least, once every five (5) years. 
WPC performs catch basin cleaning to provide a clear pathway for water to enter the sewer system. WPC 
typically cleans more than ten thousand (10,000) catch basins per year. The schedule of catch basin 
cleaning is based on known problem areas, visual observation and by requests.  WPC ’s goal is to 
increase catch basin cleaning so that each catch basin is cleaned, at least, once every three (3) years. 
The City Division of Streets contributes to WPC preventative maintenance program by performing all of 
the street cleaning in the City.  
WPC performs routine inspections of its sewer lines through a staff of house connection inspectors  who 
investigate any complaint and determine the process of resolution, including follow  up. They also make 
visual inspections while on rounds to detect problems in the sewer lines including (among other items) 
observations of sunken or flooded areas, ground cracks along pipe routes, damage to special structures 
and manholes, manhole covers above or below pavement levels, and evidence of flooding or seepage 
from sewers. This information is recorded in the City’s CMMS which is also used to log customer service 
requests and complaints and to generate and manage maintenance work orders and performance 
measures. 
Based on the available information, WPC’s maintenance crews are deployed to determine the problem 
and to perform necessary repairs. Cleaning and closed circuit television (CCTV) inspections are 
conducted and a permanent video log of the inspections is kept for further study. WPC immediately 
repairs problems with in-house staff. Maintenance crews are dispatched by a priority rating system with 
customer “no relief” status given the highest priority. For large scale emergencies, WPC employs on-call 
contractors to insure immediate repairs. 
WPC received 4,526 sewer service requests in 2013 and 4,430 requests in 2014. In 2015, approximately 
4,357 sewer service requests were recorded and investigated by WPC. Sewer flow issues, including 
sewer back up and flooding, accounted for approximately twenty-six percent (26%) of these calls. Of the 
complaints received, many were attributable to poor private lateral conditions. Typically, the private 
laterals account for the majority of the poor sewer conditions due to lack of maintenance on the 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 4-2  
homeowners’ part as well as the increased vulnerability of the laterals due to root intrusion. The 
remainder of the complaints were to report, or to request, an investigation related to blocked catch basins, 
missing or broken manhole covers, sewer cave-ins, or damaged catch basins. 
Some of the calls or requests were to report an illicit discharge to the System, such as a chemical spill, 
septage discharge or the presence of chemical odors. Some were for illegal dumping into the System 
such as dumping of debris.  
The classifications of calls and requests are generally typical from year to year. After the receipt of a call 
or a service request, WPC issues a work order for investigation of the request. The work order may be 
followed by several other work orders based on the need for the particular investigation. A service call 
may generate more than three work orders depending on the situation. 
WPC reports on its maintenance performance to NEORSD on an annual basis. Table 4-1 provides a 
summary of WPC’s key maintenance performance measures since 2011.

As illustrated above, the performance metric for any line item varies from year to year depending on the 
priority needs of the System which, in turn, are affected by customer service requests, weather 
conditions, emergencies and availability of equipment. For example, in 2012 there was an increased need 
to clean catch basins. Whereas in 2013, there was an increased need for cleaning and televising sewer 
lines. In 2014 and 2015, WPC was able to increase the number of catch basin brick work and house 
connection repairs.

WPC also maintains records relating to the a) average number of days to complete house connection 
repair work; b) average number of days to complete catch basin repair work; and c) average response 
time for customer service complaints. WPC uses this to benchmark and improve future performance. On 
average, WPC responds to customer complaints within seventy-five (75) minutes and completes repair 
work within two (2) weeks.  
WPC also conducts regular inspection of its pump stations including performing preventative 
maintenance and repair and replacement of components as needed for proper operations and to maintain 
redundancy. 
WPC’s historical operation and maintenance efforts have served to fulfill customer requests and meet the 
immediate needs of the System. WPC has established a proactive approach to meet both the current and 
long-term needs of the System. To assist in implementing this approach, WPC received approval for the 
implementation of a new fixed charge component to the sewer rate beginning in FY2015. A discussion of 
the rates and charges is presented in Section 7 of this Report. The new fixed charge was established to 
provide for increased investment in infrastructure, which will facilitate replacement of aging sewers and 
related equipment. This will result in fewer emergency repairs and an increase in proactive cleaning and 
inspections.   
4.4 Key Operating Permits and Regulatory Status 
Regulations affecting the collection and discharge of wastewater from WPC are contained in the City’s 
Community Discharge Permits with NEORSD and its Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit. NEORSD discharge 
permits regulate the sanitary and the combined sanitary and storm sewers. These permits do not contain 
any expiration date, but are subject to modifications as necessary. Pursuant to th ese discharge permits, 
WPC is required to submit an Annual Compliance Report Checklist to NEORSD . The compliance report 
checklist demonstrates WPC’s compliance with the permit and NEORSD’s best management practice 
(BMP) guidelines. NEORSD’s BMP guidelines contain five (5) key BMPs: 
• BMP 1: General Conditions 
• BMP 2: Operation and Maintenance and Inspection Program 
• BMP 3: Source Control 
• BMP 4: Record System 
• BMP 5: BMP Frequencies 
o Sewer System Cleaning 
o Sewer System Inspection 
o Catch Basin Cleaning 
o Street Sweeping 
o Storage Device Cleaning 
o Leaf Pickup 
o Pump Station Operations 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 4-4  
Discharge of stormwater for WPC is regulated by the City’s Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit. As discussed 
in Section 4, only a small portion of the System consists of separated storm sewers. The majority of the 
System is combined storm and sewer system that is regulated under the previously discussed discharge 
permits.  A new Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit was issued on September 11, 2014. Key requirements of 
the permit include compliance with the Six Minimum Control Measures and submission of annual reports 
to the Ohio Environmental Protection Agency (OEPA) on compliance activities as previously discussed in 
Section 3.2.2. 
4.4.1 Regulatory Compliance 
WPC is not under any administrative orders, and to the best of our knowledge, there are no issued 
notices of violations. NEORSD, however, is under a Consent Order to eliminate combined sewer 
overflows and improve water quality in Lake Erie through the implementation of its LTCP.  
WPC is implementing NEORSD best management practices (BMP) included in its permits and reporting 
on its compliance to NEORSD through submission of its Annual Compliance Report Check list as required 
by its permits. WPC is also supporting NEORSD in implementing its LTCP. The BMPs included in WPC’s 
discharge permits provide various BMP frequency guidelines, such as cleaning of sewers once every five 
(5) years. These guidelines represent goals for WPC, and are not a condition or requirement of the 
permits.  
With respect to its Ohio EPA NPDES MS4 permit for stormwater, WPC document s its compliance 
activities in its annual reports to the Ohio EPA. Based on a review of these reports, WPC appears to be in 
compliance with the requirements.   
At this time, there are no other known regulations forecasted to be promulgated in the near future that 
would have a significant impact on WPC’s operations, or would require significant capital expenditures in 
addition to those already anticipated by WPC. As a condition of WPC’s discharge permit, NEORSD has 
the ability to impose peak flow limits, which could require significant capital investment in excess of 
currently contemplated capital expenditures. At this time, there is no indication that NEORSD would 
impose any such limits. See Section 2 regarding WPC and coordination with NEORSD.  
4.5 Discussion 
WPC maintains a sewer system preventative maintenance program that includes implementation of  
BMPs and is in compliance with its regulatory permits. As part of these BMPs, the permits identify key 
goals and frequencies to measure BMP achievements. These goals and frequencies are not 
requirements, but guidelines. WPC has established System BMP goals that appear to appropriately 
balance costs and benefits and a sound basis for measurement of these goals. Historically, WPC’s 
program focused first on addressing any complaints and known problem areas and second on conducting 
preventative maintenance. While these priorities remain, WPC is increasing its resources (both through 
establishment of the new fixed charge to fund capital, and through increased staffing for maintenance and 
repairs) to provide for increased preventative maintenance and a higher rate of replacement of sewers 
and equipment that are past their useful lives. WPC’s continued investment in capital and staffing will 
allow WPC to substantially achieve the BMP goals within the forecast period.

5      CONDITION OF SYSTEM 
5.1 Condition Assessment Approach 
Arcadis conducted a condition assessment review of the System in January 2016 and February 2016 in 
connection with the proposed Series 2016 Bond issuance. The condition assessment review included site 
visits to a representative number of pump stations and storm facilities and a desk -top review of available 
information regarding the age and condition of buried infrastructure (linear assets)  and equipment used to 
maintain the System. The condition assessment also included a review of existing reports provided by 
WPC, discussions and interviews with WPC staff, and confirmation of the visual observations made 
during the limited field visits of the facilities. The key purpose of this condition review was to confirm 
anticipated conditions, assess general maintenance and repair of the S ystem, and assess the adequacy 
of WPC’s proposed capital improvement plan.  
The critical assets of WPC include twelve (12
1) pump stations. The condition assessment focused 
primarily on a limited field inspection of these pump stations that occurred during the week of January 6, 
2016.  During these site visits, issues facing WPC were discussed, including the steps being taken to 
address these issues. The condition of the pump stations and ancillary equipment also was discussed. 
Key findings are discussed in subsequent sections.  
For buried infrastructure (i.e., sewer interceptors, storm sewers, sanitary and combined sewers, laterals, 
force mains, manholes, catch basins, etc.) and the maintenance equipment, the condition assessment 
relied on existing information provided by WPC. This included information regarding the type, age and 
reported condition of maintenance equipment and preliminary GIS information regarding the age and 
materials of pipes to the extent that information is available, as well as reports made available regarding 
compliance activities. No field investigations were conducted on the buried infrastructure or maintenance 
equipment. Arcadis has no reason to question the soundness of the information provided by WPC based 
on historical knowledge of the WPC System, and as such, accepted the information as provided.  
The condition assessment of the critical above-ground assets was based on numerical ratings within the 
following categories.  
• Reliability 
• Operations and maintenance (O&M) performance 
• Capacity 
• Regulatory Compliance 
Using the above categories, an overall risk rating was assigned to each of the pump stations. The risk 
ratings for each of the above four categories are outlined in Table 5-1. The risk rating assigned to each 
pump station is presented in Section 5-2 following the description of the pump stations. 
1 WPC was originally responsible for 15 pump stations. However, 3 will be transferred to NEORSD by  May 15, 2016 as discussed in 
Section 2.6.

When considering the rating assigned to a critical asset, the criticality of that asset was also considered. 
For assets that are critical to the overall operation and regulatory compliance of the facility, the allowable 
risk is small. Thus, highly critical assets would tend to be given more stringent ratings.  
5.2 Condition of Sewage Pumping Stations 
Limited field visits to twelve (12) remote sewage pump stations were conducted beginning on January 6, 
2016. In general, based on our limited visual inspection during these site visits, it appears that most of 
WPC’s pumping stations are in fair to good physical condition, fairly reliable, and have adequate hydraulic 
capacity. Appendix D, Figure D-3 provides a map that shows the relative location of WPC’s pump stations 
within System. The following provides a description of the pump stations and their risk review score (see 
Table 5-3). 
WPC utilizes two distinct types of sewage pumping stations. All the stations are duplex stations, either of 
the centrifugal suction lift type, or the centrifugal flooded suction type. The suction lift stations are typically 
housed in an above-ground fiberglass enclosure over a precast concrete wet well. The pumping 
equipment, controls, valves and piping are all housed above ground in the enclosure. The centrifugal 
flooded suction type stations utilize a pre-fabricated “can” station, which includes a dry well containing the 
pumps, controls and valves and a separate wet well that collects the wastewater before pumping.  
All of WPC’s pump stations are relatively small in size (under 700 gallon per minute capacity), with pump 
inlets of either four (4) inch or six (6) inch suction pipe size. With the exception of the Burke Lakefront 
Airport Pump Station; most were constructed in the late 1980s and 1990s, and are within the expected 
design lives for the facilities. WPC has no ownership responsibilities of the Burke Lakefront Airport Pump 
Station. Another City department retains such ownership, but WPC is responsible for operations and 
maintenance of the station. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 5-2  
WPC pump stations are generally reliable and no major issues are reported. The Incinerator Pump 
Station is essentially new, having been replaced with all new components in 2015; however, the stations 
that are forty (40) or more years old, such as the pump stations located at Nottingham Road, Panna 
Lane, and Harsax Avenue, will require significant upgrades in the next few years.   
WPC’s pumping stations have two pumps; only one of which is required for normal peak conditions.  
During severe wet weather events, however, both pumps may need to operate to meet peak conditions 
due to excessive inflow and infiltration (I/I) into the System. WPC also has portable pumps that are 
transported and set up at pump stations to assist with pumping the flow during wet weather events.   The 
vast majority of pumping stations have adequate, and even excess capacity, and thus run infrequently. 
Table 5-2 identifies the run times of the pump stations under average day dry weather conditions.

WPC utilizes a special design of its duplex pumping systems, which consists of one of the two duplex 
pumps being equipped with both an electric motor, as well as an internal combustion engine operating on 
natural gas. This engine driven pump, when operated during a power loss event, would produce 
adequate power to operate the system controls including telemetry and operate a single pump to maintain 
system operations. Because the pump stations are equipped with these engine driven pumps, back -up 
generators are not required. WPC also can provide portable pumps during power outages to provide 
redundancy to the affected pump stations.

WPC has two maintenance contracts in place to provide service and repair on all of its pump stations. 
These service contracts appear to be effective at maintaining the pump stations and associated telemetry 
and control systems since each are in good working condition.  
In order to remotely monitor the pumping stations, all of the stations are equipped with radio telemetry to 
transmit critical signals and alarms to WPC’s Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA) system.  
Should this radio system fail, WPC dispatches crews to monitor the pump stations on a daily basis. 
While many of the pumping stations are in residential neighborhoods, WPC does not report any

As noted, the above ratings reflect the general condition of the pump stations. For the most part, the 
pump stations appear to be reliable; however a few present potential risks and require additional 
engineering investigations to develop capital improvement requirements and recommendations.  Such 
improvement requirements could require up to $2 million of capital investment over the next five (5) years.   
At this time, WPC does not have any specifically identified capital projects to address pump station 
upgrades. WPC, however, does have undesignated funding set aside in its five-year capital plan to 
address future capital improvement requirements. Such funding is available for improvements to upgrade 
the condition of WPC’s pump stations. Details of the capital plan are provided in Section 6. 
5.3 Condition of the Collection System  
As presented in Section 3 of this Report, the estimated average age of the WPC collection system is 
eighty (80) years, and it is estimated that approximately twenty-seven percent (27%) of the system is 
older than one hundred (100) years.  
Over the past five (5) years, WPC has invested approximately $5 million per year on a cash basis for its 
capital program, which includes renewal and replacement of its aging infrastructure. Recognizing that an 
increased level of investment is needed to preserve the long-term reliability of its assets, it is embarking 
on an accelerated program to increase targeted investment in renewal and replacement. Beginning in 
FY2016, WPC’s operating budget includes an appropriation of $1 million each year for a five (5) year 
period to conduct sewer system evaluation surveys (SSESs) to identify sewer pipes in need of repair and 
replacement. The SSES includes infrastructure inspections, condition assessment, flow monitoring, 
smoke and dye testing and a public information program. A hydraulic sewer computer model also will be 
developed for sewer pipes ten (10) inches in diameter and greater, along with associated rehabilitation 
recommendations, including criticality evaluation of the risks and challenges. In addition, WPC’s capital 
budget, which has been increased to an average of $12.8 million per year for the next five (5) years, 
includes the hiring of a Program Manager (PMT project) to assist WPC in the implementation of its 
targeted capital plan. This capital plan represents more than a doubling of historic al investment into the 
System. Section 6 presents additional details regarding WPC’s capital plan. 
WPC is serving its customers and maintaining compliance with its permit requirements.  A review of 
customer service requests indicates that approximately twenty percent (20%) of the requests are 
potentially associated with collapses and breaks due to deteriorated pipe conditions. WPC conducts 
CCTV inspection of pipes to examine sewers/connections as these service requests are called in by 
residents.  While the number of service requests has declined over the past three (3) years, the number 
of repairs has increased over the past two (2) years. The recent increase in repairs is due in part to WPC 
proactively addressing some deferred maintenance, but also may be due to increased requirements 
associated with the aging infrastructure. 
WPC also undertakes ongoing condition assessments, as well as contracting for professional engineering 
services to conduct comprehensive SSES of known problem areas. The most recent of such studies is a 
Technical Report dated February 2014 for the East 185th Street/Lakeshore Blvd Area SSES . Moving 
forward, WPC has allocated in its operating budget an annual expenditure of $1 million per year to 
conduct SSESs and develop a targeted capital improvement plan. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 5-5  
The East 185th St./Lakeshore Blvd. study area is one of the few areas in the City with separated sewers. 
The local sanitary sewer system in the area conveys flow to the Euclid Creek Pump Station through the 
Lakeshore Boulevard Interceptor Sewer.  In 2015, NEORSD increased the capacity of the system by 
upgrading the Euclid Creek Pump Station and constructing a new relief sewer.   
Although NEORSD has increased the capacity of the Euclid Creek Pump Station and constructed the 
new relief sewer, the study identified that additional improvements are needed within the WPC collection 
system to reduce wet weather flows. Several alternatives were presented with the most cost effective 
alternative being the construction of a conveyance/relief sewer and rehabilitation of the existing sewers  at 
an estimated cost of $2.7 million. WPC is finalizing its plan for the East 185th Street/Lakeshore Boulevard 
study area, and anticipates undertaking the major capital requirements of the project in FY2018 and 
FY2019. In the meantime, WPC is undertaking a number of improvements along Euclid Creek as part of 
its ongoing repair program and capital projects budget for catch basins and manholes .  
5.4 Condition of Collection System Equipment 
WPC maintains a fleet of more than eighty (80) vehicles ranging from pickup trucks used by supervisors 
and staff to conduct inspections and respond to complaints; to heavy equipment used by staff to respond 
to emergencies. Approximately half of the vehicles are used daily to maintain the System. Figure 5-1 
provides a summary status of the key equipment needed to maintain the S ystem, including number of 
allotted vehicles (includes all planned vehicles regardless of operational status), number in f air-to-good 
operational condition, and average number deployed on a daily basis. In most instances sufficient 
equipment in good operational condition were available to meet the System demands. This was not the 
case for the vac-all and jet-vac vehicles, where equipment deemed to be in poor or unreliable condition 
needed to be deployed to meet the System needs.  
The average age of the vehicles listed in Figure 5-1 is 8 years. WPC typically establishes a ten (10) year 
life for vehicles. The vehicles that are in poor condition are reportedly being scheduled for replacement as 
budget permits. In the meantime, they serve as backup vehicles. WPC purchased twelve (12) new 
vehicles in 2014, and has budgeted $1.9 million in its FY2016 capital budget for the purchase and/or 
lease of five (5) new vacuum-trucks. WPC’s capital budget for the next five (5) years includes a total of 
$6.5 million for collection system equipment to be funded with cash to meet its vehicle allocation plan.  
WPC’s ability to address sewer system investigations and repairs in the past has been limited by the 
availability of good operating vehicles and maintenance equipment. The acquisition of the twelve ( 12) 
new vehicles in 2014 resulted in an increase in completed repairs. The equipment allocation established 
should serve to further increase preventative maintenance activity, television inspections and completion 
of repairs.
