z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 5-6  
 
Figure 5-1.  Summary Status of Key Equipment Needed to Maintain the System 
5.5 Discussion 
Based on January 2016 visual inspections, Arcadis has made some observations of the System that, if 
addressed, could further improve facility performance and operations. Many of these already are 
addressed in WPC’s five-year capital plan. They include:  
• The wastewater and stormwater collection system has an average age of approximately eighty 
(80) years with parts of the system exceeding the typical useful life. Conducting SSESs and 
detailed investigation of customer service requests will help to identify priorities for renewal and 
replacement. The use of the CMMS and GIS will facilitate development of a comprehensive asset 
management program, and the PMT Project should result in the cost effective and efficient 
implementation of WPC’s capital improvement plan. WPC should further target increasing its 
capital expenditures over the long term, with a goal of renewal and replacement of one percent 
(1%) of its system per year, subject to results of ongoing sewer inspections. This likely will require 
a continued annual capital investment at least equal to that of the five-year plan beyond FY2020.  
• WPC conducts regular inspection and preventative maintenance of the pump stations to ensure 
operability.  Several pump stations (Burke Lakefront Airport Station, Nottingham Road Station 
and Panna Lane Station), however, represent a high priority for renewal and replacement 
investment to minimize potential risks. The Nottingham Road Station and Lakefront Airport 
Station likely will require replacement within the next five (5) years. Capital improvements for the 
Burke Lakefront Airport Station, however, remain the Department of Port Control’s responsibility.  
The E37th Street Station, Harsax Avenue Station and Spring Hill Station are not that old, but will 
require some refurbishment. The cost of these improvements could be up to $2 million. WPC will 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 5-7  
evaluate the refurbishment needs of these pump stations and implement the needed 
improvements over the next five (5) years. It is anticipated that funding for the improvements will 
come from WPC’s undesignated project allocation contained in its five- year plan. 
• The allocation of capital funds established for maintenance equipment appears sufficient to meet 
the needs of the System. Much of the existing equipment will require replacement. The capital 
plan addresses these requirements. 
Overall, the System appears to have sufficient capacity to meet current and projected future wastewater 
needs of the service area.  Based on the limited visual observations and review of information, the 
System appears to be functioning satisfactorily. Portions of the System are past their useful life and 
therefore poses additional risk for potential sewer line failures.  The WPC capital plan has been 
developed with a focus on minimizing any such risks. 
Available data indicates that WPC is operating and maintaining the System in general compliance with its 
permit requirements with NEORSD and the conditions of its MS4 stormwater permit. Based on our 
observations and discussions with WPC staff, operation and maintenance of the System continues to be 
enhanced through implementation of technology and improved information management systems , 
increases in staff for operations, and increased capital investment.  
With respect to the pump stations, WPC’s pump stations appear to be reliable and have sufficient 
capacity. Several pump stations present some potential risk and require investment; however, all of the 
pump stations are relatively small and run only a few hours per day.  
While it is difficult to assess the condition of the collection system, WPC understands the risks of its older 
system, and is therefore undertaking SSESs to investigate its condition and develop cost effective 
renewal and replacement plans.  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 5-8  
6      CAPITAL IMPROVEMENT PROGRAM 
Arcadis was provided with the five-year capital plan for WPC, which covers the fiscal years 2016 through 
2020. The fiscal year 2015 plan was also provided for reference. This plan is provided as Appendix B and 
summarized below.  
6.1 Past Capital Improvements 
WPC historically employed a pay-as-you-go capital improvement plan, supplemented with grants and low 
cost loans from the Ohio Public Works Commission (OPWC) and Ohio Water Development Authority 
(OWDA) for eligible projects.  Past improvement efforts focused primarily on addressing both street and 
basement flooding, acquiring equipment needed to maintain the System and implementing information 
technology systems to better manage its assets. For example, WPC implemented Cityworks as its CMMS 
and integrated the City’s GIS to view storm and wastewater assets and analyzing preventive maintenance 
issues without being on site.  WPC prioritized its capital improvement program based on known problem 
areas, results of sewer investigations, customer surveys, service calls and complaints and data available 
from its information management systems.  Past CIPs included construction of relief main sewers, 
replacement of collapsed and deteriorated sewers, drainage improvements to prevent flooding and lining 
of storm and sanitary sewers.  Table 6-1 presents a summary of the historical annual level of capital 
expenditure on the System:

The five-year capital plan represents WPC’s anticipated plan based on the information available as of 
January 2016. WPC is currently procuring a professional capital improvements manager (PMT project) 
and conducting SSESs to refine the proposed plan. Therefore, the five-year plan may be subject to 
change as new information becomes available. WPC has established the “undesignated” category to 
account for unknowns and provide a funding allocation to address SSES recommendations  and pump 
station improvement requirements.  
6.3.1 Stormwater System – Planned Improvements 
A total of $4.75 million is budgeted for stormwater system upgrades over the next five (5) years. Of this 
amount, $2.5 million is budgeted to remove shoaling deposits and in stream vegetation; and provide 
stream bank stabilization along Euclid Creek pursuant to the agreement reached with the USACOE dated 
March 27, 2015.  The remainder is for annual catch basin and manhole rehabilitation and reconstruction 
throughout the System. The five-year capital plan also includes $2.5 million in sewer work on roadway 
projects. These projects include approximately $0.5 million per year of sewer and storm drainage 
improvements at various locations within the City that are coordinated with the City’s Public Works 
Department to enhance efficiency of operations. A more detailed description of these projects is provided 
in Appendix B. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 6-4  
As described in Section 2.6, NEORSD will implement its stormwater management user charge to recover 
NEORSD expenses related to management of combined stormwater interceptors  and overflows and 
implementation of green infrastructure and other initiatives in compliance with its NPDES Permit and its 
approved LTCP. The City and NEORSD are in discussions regarding NEORSD potential assistance in 
funding WPC stormwater projects through a portion of revenues collected by NEORSD through its 
stormwater user charge. Options for such funding assistance may include NEORSD providing funding for 
qualifying stormwater projects undertaken by the City. At this time, however, no such funding has been 
included in the CIP. Once this funding becomes available, it is anticipated that additional stormwater 
projects will be added to the CIP as appropriate. 
6.3.2 Wastewater Collection System – Planned Improvements 
The majority of WPC’s five-year capital budget is related to sewer replacement projects. Of the $28.7 
million five-year expenditure identified under the category Sewer Replacement, approximately $14 million 
is budgeted for ongoing annual sewer replacements, sewer lining, and service connection replacements 
at various locations throughout the City. The remainder consists of specific projects related to 
rehabilitation and replacement of aging sewers that are anticipated to be funded from the proceeds of the 
Series 2016 Bonds or future bonds.  
In addition to the above, the plan also includes $11.9 million under the Undesignated Projects category. 
WPC, through its operating budget, will hire professional engineers to conduct SSESs of the System to 
assess the condition of the collection system and identify targeted improvements. The recommended 
capital improvements from these SSESs will be funded through the undesignated projects budget. Capital 
improvements identified to upgrade WPC pump stations and address other improvements identified as a 
result of condition assessments would also be funded from this category. 
6.3.3 Building and Other Planned Improvements 
The five-year capital plan includes $16.2 million in capital expenditures for building and other 
improvements. Of this amount, $0.4 million represents WPC’s continued investment in technology, $6.5 
million in equipment to maintain the System (both to be funded with cash), $6.8 million for program 
management to ensure implementation of a cost effective capital improvement program, and $2.5 million 
in professional services for sewer design and related services (to be funded with revenue bonds).  
6.4 Discussion 
Our review of the proposed capital improvements projects resulted in the following findings:  
1. Contracts for Sewer Replacement, Sewer Lining, and Sewer Connections represent a 
continuation of efforts by WPC from the last two (2) years. We are of the opinion that that these 
services provided good value to WPC and that it is reasonable for WPC to appropriate additional 
funds to continue receiving these valued services.  
2. The remaining capital projects proposed for 2016, 2017 and 2018 appear to have been prepared 
with reasonable judgment to the scope of the proposed improvements and to the value of the 
anticipated construction costs. We are of the opinion that the proposed costs are equivalent to the 
proposed scope of these projects.  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 6-5  
It is anticipated that WPC will continue its practice of updating its five-year capital plan as soon as the 
results of ongoing studies, such as the SSESs, are completed and in no event less than once per year. 
WPC is also expected to make the necessary changes to the capital plan and not delay acquisition of 
funding to support the required capital projects.

7      CUSTOMER STATISTICS AND SEWER USE RATES 
7.1 Customer Base 
The City has a population of approximately 390,000 (based on 2010 U.S. Census Bureau statistics) and 
is the 48th largest city in the US, and the second largest in Ohio. WPC provides services to approximately 
126,000 active metered water connections that serve all residential, commercial, and industrial, 
government and non-profit customers. Table 7-1 illustrates the current number of active water metered 
accounts broken down by meter size. Fewer than ten (10) customers in the southwest side of the City are 
served by septic systems.

In 2014, WPC experienced a slight increase in billable consumption. This increase was due in part to the 
Division of Water implementing an automated meter reading (AMR) system, which served to reduce the 
number of estimated bills and improve meter reading accuracy. This is anticipated to be a one-time 
increase in response to the improved AMR system. Over the long-term however, consumption per 
account is anticipated to decrease in response to water conservation efforts. This reduction is offset 
somewhat by WPC’s minimum bill policy as described in Section 7.2.  
WPC is projecting continued decreases in consumption in FY2016 through FY2020. A two and two-tenths 
percent (2.2%) annual decrease in consumption billing revenue is projected throughout the planning 
period to account for potential decreases in customer usage and other unknowns . This projection is 
consistent with the Division of Water’s projections for water consumption. With respect to number of 
billing customers, the total number of customers is projected to remain static during the forecast period. 
The number of customers is based on buildings with metered water service that are connected to the 
System. As long as the buildings are connected to the System they will continue to be billed a fixed 
charge regardless of the amount of water consumed. WPC does not anticipate any net disconnection of 
buildings or establishments from its System during the forecast period.  A summary of the projected fixed

Although the City has seen significant population decline for more than a decade, in large part due to 
declines in large industry and manufacturing jobs, that decline is stabilizing as the City has become more 
diversified. The City’s Top Ten Customers represent primarily service companies. 
The City’s unemployment rate, as of December 2015, was slightly higher than the State of Ohio and 
national averages (at approximately six and nine-tenths percent (6.9%)), but remains lower than 
unemployment rates in 2010, which were at ten and eight-tenths percent (10.8%).  As a result, we believe 
that WPC currently has a stable and diverse customer base, and the projected customer declines are 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 7-3  
likely overstated. The median household income of $26,179 per household in the City (2014 census 
data), however, remains significantly lower than the State of Ohio average of $48,849 (2014 census 
data). Maintaining affordable rates remains a priority for the City. It is for this reason that WPC provides a 
homestead rate as discussed further in the next sections. 
7.2 User Rates and Charges 
WPC is responsible for establishing sewer rates and other fees and charges for its customers, subject to 
approval by the Board of Control and City Council. Pursuant to Section 112 Fixation of Utility Rates of the 
City Charter: “Rates for the service or products of all non-tax supported public utilities, owned and 
operated by the City which are managed and supervised by the Director of Public Utilities, shall be fixed 
by the Board of Control, subject, however to approval by Council.”  Furthermore, in Section 80 Board of 
Control of the City Charter: “The Mayor and the directors of the several departments, whether established 
by this Charter or by ordinance, shall constitute a Board of Control. The Mayor shall be ex -officio 
President of the Board. The vote of a majority of all members of the Board shall be necessary to the 
adoption of any question, motion or order. All votes shall be by “yeas” and “nays” and entered on the 
record. All meetings of the Board shall be public, a record of its proceedings shall be kept, and an 
abstract of its proceedings shall be printed in the City Record. 
The rates must be at sufficient levels to pay for O&M costs of the System, and debt service on 
outstanding debt, and to provide for appropriate contingency, coverage, and reserves in accordance with 
the requirements of the Trust Agreement and General Bond Ordinance. User charges are set after 
accounting for other revenue, collection rate assumptions, and requirements for debt service coverage 
and contingency reserves. 
Table 7-5 shows the historical user rates for WPC for FY2011 through FY2015. The rates include two key 
charge components: 
• User Consumption Charges: Historically, WPC relied solely on user charges that were based 
on each customer’s billable metered water consumption. Under this consumption charge 
component, customers are charged the same rate per MCF of metered water consumption.   The 
only exception is that certain customers pay a discounted Homestead rate if they are eligible and 
have been approved based on established economic and social criteria. The Homestead rate 
provides customers with a discounted rate which is approximately forty percent (40%) lower than 
the regular rate to maintain affordability of such rates. The consumption charge also includes a 
minimum bill charge based on a minimum consumption of one MCF per quarter.  
• Fixed Meter Charges: Beginning in FY2015, WPC instituted a new fixed charge component that 
varies based on the size of the customer’s incoming water meter service. Billing of customers for 
this new fixed charge began during the second quarter of FY2015. See Table 7-6 for a 
breakdown of charges by meter size. The fixed charge is in addition to the consumption charge 
and was instituted to address the costs of maintaining the infrastructure of the System. The fixed 
charge is assessed even if the customer had zero water consumption. Similar to  the consumption 
charge, a forty percent (40%) discounted Homestead fixed charge rate is available for qualifying 
customers to maintain affordability of the rates.  
 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 7-4

MCF for regular customers and $7.43 per MCF for homestead customers. In 2015, the fixed charge 
component was implemented, while the unit consumption rate remained the same as in previous years.

7.3 Billing and Collection 
In accordance with WPC’s billing policies, customers are billed quarterly based on their meter size and 
metered water consumption. Bills are issued by the City’s Division of Water on behalf of WPC. The 
Division of Water charges WPC its allocable share of the cost of billing services provided based on the 
Division of Water’s cost and number of bills issued. Billing, collections and customer service are included 
in the services provided by the Division of Water. Consistent with historical collection rates, WPC 
anticipates an average annual collection rate of ninety percent (90%).  
The Division of Water, as billing agent for WPC, anticipates changing from quarterly billing to monthly 
billing in FY2017 in response to customer requests. While the overall charges from the Division of Water 
are anticipated to increase commensurate with increased costs associated with more frequent printing 
and postage costs, the charges per bill will decrease due to frequency. Furthermore, because no increase 
in staffing is anticipated to be required and the increased postage and printing costs will be split between 
WPC, Water and Waste Collection, the net increase in WPC’s share of the cost of billing services due to 
changing to monthly billing is anticipated to be minimal. A small increase in billing costs is projected to be 
incurred in FY2017 and has been included in WPC’s forecast.

8      FINANCIAL FEASIBILITY 
8.1 Overview 
As part of this Report, a financial plan and forecast were prepared for WPC for FY2016 through FY2020. 
The purpose of this section is to present the financial plan and forecast, the projection of revenues and 
expenses, debt service coverage, and to document the assumptions used in the preparation of the 
forecast in order to provide an engineer’s opinion as to the financial feasibility of the Series 2016 Bonds.   
The financial forecast represents an estimate of the probable results of operations and reflects WPC’s 
judgment as to the most likely set of conditions and course of action based upon present circumstances. 
Arcadis worked closely with WPC to obtain the information necessary to prepare the financial forecast, 
and various financial and system information was provided by WPC to support its development.

shown in Table 8-1, a significant increase in sewer user charge revenue was realized in FY2015 as a 
result of the implementation of the Fixed Charge component of the rate structure to fund infrastructure 
costs.

charges include billing services provided by the Division of Water, financial services provided by Division 
of Fiscal Control, vehicle maintenance provided by the Division of Motor Vehicle Maintenance and other 
administrative services (human resources, information technology and public relations support) provided 
by various other City divisions.

WPC plans to fund the capital plan described in Section 6 with a mix of cash and debt, as summarized in

cash. In FY2019 and FY2020, WPC anticipates funding its CIP with a combination of cash and additional 
revenue bonds. To the extent that WPC can secure grants and loans from other sources, this will serve to 
expedite the capital plan and offset the need to issue additional revenue bonds. The projections,

assumptions associated with these projections include:

In addition to the above, the forecast includes maintenance of a $1 million dollar contingency fund, six (6) 
months of cash reserves, and a debt service reserve fund for all revenue bond debt.  The debt service 
reserve for the Series 2016 Bonds was assumed to be capitalized as part of the issuance of the Series 
2016 Bonds.  
For the purposes of projecting estimated new debt service anticipated to be required beginning in 
FY2019, an interest rate of five percent (5%) and an amortization period of thirty (30) years was 
assumed.  In lieu of additional revenue bond issues, however, WPC intends to pursue grants and low 
interest loans for projects as they become available. This will include grants and loans anticipated to be 
available from NEORSD for stormwater projects in the near future.   
8.3.5 Debt Service Coverage Requirements 
The Trust Agreement and General Bond Ordinance contain specific debt service coverage requirements 
that must be met by WPC. Specifically, the rate covenant requires that the City set its rates so as to 
cause its Net Revenues to meet the greater of a) one hundred twenty percent (120%) of the annual debt 
service on WPC’s outstanding Bonds or b) one hundred percent (100%) of the sum of the outstanding 
debt including any required deposits to reserves.  Projected debt service coverage results are presented 
in Table 8-6, and are anticipated to be sufficient to satisfy the requirements of Section 20 (c) and (d). 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx 8-6  
8.3.6 WPC Management Policies 
WPC anticipates funding the majority of its capital plan with revenue bonds and low cost loans or grants as 
they become available, and using cash for equipment and technology investments and repairs as needed.  
WPC has maintained operating reserves to address potential liquidity concerns and improve the ability of 
the utility to absorb potential short-term operating deficits in months when billed consumption may decline 
and where fixed costs are high. The City has also covenanted in the Trust Agreement to maintain a 
Contingency Fund to further improve its ability to respond to emergencies. For the purpose of projections 
included in Table 8-6, a minimum operating reserve target equal to six (6) months (180 days)  of annual 
O&M expenses was assumed. These reserves are in addition to the Contingency Fund Requirement, which 
has been established in the General Bond Ordinance at a minimum of $1,000,000.    
In addition to the rate covenant requirements described in this Report, WPC has established an internal 
management target for debt service coverage of 150 percent.  
8.4 Cash Flow Projection  
Presented in Table 8-6, are financial projections for WPC for the period of FY2016 through FY2020. 
Notes for each of the line items in Table 8-6 are presented in Appendix C. Based on the projections, it is 
anticipated that WPC will achieve its debt service coverage requirements in FY2016 through FY2019 with 
the sewer user rate increases that have been adopted. It is also anticipated that the City will need to 
approve an additional sewer rate increase in FY2020 to fund its proposed capital improvement plan and 
meet its debt service coverage requirements for FY2020. On Table 8-6 a rate increase of 4.5 percent is 
assumed for FY2020 and based on the revenue and expense projections results in a debt service 
coverage ratio of 164 percent. This targeted rate increase has not yet been formally proposed to, and will 
require approval by, City Council. A comprehensive rate study will be undertaken in 2019 to establish the 
recommended rates for FY2020 through FY2025.  
These projections reflect WPC’s views and assumptions with respect to future events as of the date of 
this Report, and are subject to future economic conditions and other risks and uncertainties.  Arcadis 
believes that these projections are reasonable based upon the information provided to it; however, actual 
and future results and trends could differ materially from those presented herein.  Accordingly, A rcadis 
makes no warranty or representation that the projected values or results contained in this document will 
actually be achieved.  In the event that the anticipated costs and funding levels differ from the projections 
presented herein, WPC will adjust the rates accordingly.

9      CONCLUSION 
9.1 Considerations and Assumptions 
The principal considerations and assumptions are provided throughout this Report, some of which are as 
follows: 
• Arcadis has made no determination as to the validity and enforceability of any contracts, 
agreement, existing law, rule, or regulation applicable to WPC and its operations; however, for 
purposes of this Report, we have assumed that all such contracts, agreements, laws, rules and 
regulations will be fully enforceable and complied with in accordance with their terms. 
• WPC will continue its policies of employing qualified and competent personnel; will properly 
operate and maintain the System in accordance with generally accepted engineering practices  
and all recommended operations and maintenance protocols; and operate the System in a 
prudent and sound manner.  
• NEORSD will not modify WPC’s operating permit to include peak flow restrictions that would 
result in the need for WPC to implement unplanned capital improvements, or to establish BMP 
frequency requirements (versus goals) for items such as cleaning of sewers or catch basins that 
are substantially in excess of current WPC BMP frequencies. 
• The proposed CIP reflects the anticipated requirements of the System, and the CIP is expected to 
be largely implemented by WPC as planned. 
• If any unforeseen expenses occur, which may include items such as O&M expenses and capital 
expenditures to address a change in law, increased priority or uninsured catastrophic event, WPC 
would undertake internally driven actions such as reducing non-essential programs and 
implementing cost reduction measures to cover costs associated with these expenses, or adjust 
wastewater user charges as needed to satisfy the rate covenants, as may be needed.   
• WPC will update its capital plan at least annually based on the findings and recommendations of 
the SSES studies and PMT requirements. 
• WPC will continue to control costs and implement rate increases as required to meet its 
obligations.

regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission.  As such, Arcadis is not: (a) recommending any 
action regarding municipal financial products or the issuance of municipal securities; and (b) is not acting 
as a registered municipal advisor to WPC, and does not owe a fiduciary duty to WPC pursuant to Section 
15B of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended by the Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and 
Consumer Protection Act, with respect to the information and material prepared in connection with this 
Report. WPC should discuss any information and material prepared in connection with this Report with 
any and all internal and external financial and other advisors that it may deem appropriate before acting 
on this information and material.

municipal advisor, who, during the past two years, was not associated with Arcadis, and that (b) Arcadis

municipal advisor; (ii) provide written disclosure to the municipal entity that Arcadis is not serving as a 
municipal advisor and, with respect to the municipal entity, is not subject to the statutory fiduciary duty 
applicable to municipal advisors under the Securities Exchange Act, and (iii) provide a copy of such 
disclosure to the municipal entity’s independent registered municipal advisor. Arcadis  provided such 
disclosures to WPC and its registered municipal advisor. Arcadis does not provide opinions on or 
advocate for using a financial product (issuing debt) or the choice of financial products employed. As 
such, Arcadis submitted its work products to WPC’s independent registered municipal advisor for review 
and approval. 
9.2 Conclusions 
Set forth below are the principal opinions that Arcadis has reached regarding our review of the System 
and WPC-prepared budget forecasts.  For a complete understanding of these opinions, the Report should 
be read in its entirety. 
1. The System has been maintained and operated in accordance with generally accepted utility 
standards, and notwithstanding its age, appears overall to be in good general repair and 
operating condition. WPC has taken a number of steps and is working diligently to improve 
the condition of the collection system through targeted rehabilitation and replacement of 
aging sewers. 
2. The estimated costs of the CIP developed by WPC have been prepared using sound 
estimating practices and methods.  The identified capital projects are in general alignment 
with our observed requirements for the System.  
3. The financial forecast is based upon revenue and expense projections that appear to be 
reasonable.  
4. WPC has historically funded its capital program with cash and therefore has no existing debt, 
other than approximately $753,000 in principal associated with some low and zero rate 
interest loans from OWDA and OPWC.  
5. With the rate increases that have been adopted for FY2016 through FY2019, and the 
projected rate increase needed in FY2020, the one hundred eighty (180) day cash reserve 
target and the debt service coverage ratios are expected to be achieved over the Forecast 
Period that meet or exceed those required by the General Bond Ordinance, i.e., the One 
Hundred Twenty Percent (120%) Debt Service Coverage Ratio Requirement.  
6. Based on the considerations, assumptions, and conclusions described above, the financial 
forecast presented in this Report is reasonable, and the City’s plans to meet the obligations 
of the Series 2016 Water Pollution Control Bonds are financially feasible.

Project Descriptions 
1. Euclid Creek Restoration Project (2016) 
Description: The Euclid Creek project is located on the east side of the City of Cleveland in Cuyahoga 
County.  The area of concern for this project is Euclid Creek between Lake Erie and Villaview Road.   
The original flood control project was constructed by the Works Projects Administration (WPA) in the late 
1930’s.  In 1984, the portion of the WPA project from the Lake Shore Boulevard bridge to approximately 
2,000 feet upstream, also known as the Euclid Creek Flood Control project, was redeveloped by the 
Buffalo District Corps of Engineers (COE).  The initial design of the Euclid Creek Flood Control project 
was to provide a non-damaging channel with a capacity of 10,400 cubic feet per second (cfs) throughout 
the project limits.  The upstream portion of the COE project ties into the original WPA project.  Flood 
waters due to heavy rains that occurred on May 25 and May 26, 1989 severely damaged the original 
WPA project.  This initial damage was further aggravated by additional rainfall during the period of Ma y 
31 through June 9, 1989.  The Emergency Streambank Rehabilitation project was designed and 
constructed under the supervision of the Buffalo District COE and was completed on May 29, 1992.  The 
City of Cleveland was the local sponsor and superintendent.  The City inspected the completed work and 
acknowledged satisfaction with the project.  The City accepted the project along with the required 
maintenance of the creek and its structures from the U. S. Federal Government on January 29, 1993.  
Based on annual joint inspections between the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers and the City of Cleveland, 
it has been determined that the current condition of the local flood protection project on Euclid Creek has 
major deficiencies that will adversely impact the flood control project.  In addition, the original WPA 
project has deficiencies also that need to be addressed (See photos, Attachment C).  It is increasingly 
possible that the Euclid Creek Flood Control project will not withstand a major flood event and provide the 
necessary level of protection for which the project was designed. This study resulted in a comprehensive 
understanding of a multitude of problems, some of which are: 
• Woody growth and shoaling have reduced the channel capacity therefore drastically reducing the 
level of protection. 
• Declining integrity of grouted fabric slope protection from large sediment bars with vegetation 
growth. 
• Eventual failure of the levee due to encroachment of trees and bushes. 
• Missing rip-rap and heavy vegetation and wood growth within the rip-rap. 
• Holes and undermining in the concrete slopes downstream of Villaview Road.  
Project components include removal of shoaling deposits within thickness tolerances (between 12” and 
30” above concrete liner) and in stream vegetation; stream bank stabilization; project limits from 
beginning of concrete lined channel to approx. 1,600 feet downstream of Lake Shore Blvd bridge(total 
length approx. 3,600 lf). 
 
  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx B-2  
2. Constructing and Rebuilding Catch Basins and Manholes  
This project consists of Constructing and Rebuilding Catch Basins and Manholes at Various Locations 
throughout the City of Cleveland.   
3. Constructing and Installing Replacement Sewers and Rehabilitating Existing Sewers  
This project consists of constructing and installing replacement sewers and rehabilitating existing sewers 
throughout the City of Cleveland.  Work is scheduled as needed, and mostly performed in emergency 
situations. 
4. Rehabilitating and Lining Sewers  
This project consists of rehabilitating and lining sewers at various locations in the City of Cleveland.  
5. Rehabilitating and Replacing Sewer Connections  
The work consists of rehabilitating and replacing sewer service connections at various locations 
throughout the City of Cleveland.   
6. Rocky River (2016) 
Location: Rocky River Drive between Puritas Avenue and Melgrave Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of installing approximately 1,200 feet of sanitary and 1,200 feet of storm 
sewers on Rocky River Drive, between Puritas Avenue and Laverne Avenue; and approximately 250 feet 
of sanitary and 250 feet of storm sewers on Rocky River Drive, between Sedalia Avenue and Melgrave 
Avenue. The existing sewers were built in 1926. This causes property flooding on Rocky River Drive.  
7. East 75 Street Sewer Pump Station Project (2016) 
Location: East 75 Street between Dell Avenue and Grand Avenue 
Description: The existing combined sewer on East 75 Street was built in 1903. When the Norfolk 
Southern railroad tracks and East 75 Street Bridge were constructed, the combined sewage on East 75 
Street was rerouted and connected directly to the existing Kingsbury storm culvert located under the 
railroad tracks. This is considered an illicit discharge. The project will be undertaken to correct the 
problem. This project consists of installing approximately 300 LF of combined sewer on East 75 Street, 
under existing bridge, and approximately 120 LF of sewer on East 75 Street between Woodland Avenue 
and Grand Avenue in the City of Cleveland.  The construction methods for this project include open cut 
excavation and boring/jacking. 
8. East 85 Street Sewer Project (2016) 
Location: Area bordered by East 85 Street, Crawford Road, Hough Avenue, East 105 Street and Chester 
Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of relocating the exiting Spring Brook Culvert.  
The project is located in Ward 5 in the area bordered by East 85 Street, Crawford Road, Hough Avenue, 
East 105 Street and Chester Avenue, which is a residential area. The existing culverted storm sewer 
(Spring Brook Culvert) runs under properties in this area and discharges into Doan Brook. The sewer was 
built in the early 1900’s. The sewer is structurally deteriorated. 
  
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx B-3  
9. Bryant Avenue Sewer Project (2016) 
Location: Bryant Avenue between East 105 Street and Parkwood Drive 
Description:  The project consists of replacing approximately 3,000 feet of 8” and 10” sanitary sewer and 
18” storm sewer on Bryant Avenue between East 105 Street and Parkwood Drive. The existing sewers 
were built in 1908. The sewers are structurally deteriorated. This causes basement and street flooding.  
10. East 150 Street Sewer Project (2016) 
Location: East 150 Street between St Clair Avenue and Aspinwall Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of replacing approximately 1,640 feet of 9” sanitary with a 15 inch 
sanitary sewer on East 150 Street between St Clair Avenue and Aspinwall Avenue. The existing sewers 
were built in 1906. The sewers are structurally deteriorated, which causes basement and street flooding. 
11. West 48 Street Sewer Project (2016) 
Location: Between Park Dr. and Memphis Ave 
Description:  The project consists of installing approximately 1,700 feet of storm relief sewer and 
replacing approximately 300 feet of deteriorated sewers on West 48 Street between Park Drive and 
Memphis Avenue. The existing combined sewer was built in 1916. The sewer is undersized and 
structurally deteriorated, which causes basement flooding on West 48 Street.  
12. West 134 Street Sewer Project (2016) 
Location: Between San Diego Avenue and West Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of installing approximately 900 feet of storm relief sewer on West 134 
Street, between San Diego Avenue and West Avenue. The existing combined sewer was built in 1926. 
The sewer is undersized, which causes basement flooding on West 134 Street.  
13. Dartmouth Avenue and West 165 Street Sewer Project (2017) 
Location: Dartmouth between Rocky River Drive and West 165 Street; West 165 Street between Lucille 
Avenue and Ferndale Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of replacing approximately 3,900 feet of 12” sanitary and 12” -20” storm 
main sewers on Dartmouth between Rocky River Drive and West 165 Street and West 165 Street 
between Lucille Avenue and Ferndale Avenue. The existing sewers were built in 1924. The sewers are 
structurally deteriorated, which causes basement and street flooding. 
14. East 186 Street Sewer Project (2017) 
Location: Between Invermere Avenue and Harvard Avenue 
Description:  The project consists of replacing approximately 2,000 feet of 8” sanitary and 12”, 15” 21”, 
24” and 27” storm main sewers on East 186 Street between Invermere Avenue and Harvard Road. The 
existing sewers were built in 1950. The sewers are structurally deteriorated, which causes basement and 
street flooding. 
15. East 89 Street Sewer Project (2017) 
Location: Between Woodland Avenue and Buckeye Avenue

23. Roadway Drainage (2016 – 2020) 
WPC share of Department of Transportation (DOT) project costs for drainage construction.  
24. Equipment (2016 – 2020) 
For FY2016 the equipment includes the acquisition of five new vacuum trucks. In future years, equipment 
expenditures required to continue to replace vehicles and equipment that is past its useful service life.  
25. PMT (2016 – 2020) 
In January 2016, WPC issued a request for proposals for Capital Improvements program Management 
Services. The program goals and objectives included establishment of specific levels of service for sewer 
reliability, functionality and sustainable operations. This also included program, management services 
such as quality management, Management Information System, risk management, asset management 
coordination, CIP program procedures and controls including design standards, budget assistance and 
operation management. The duration of this program is expected to last five (5) years starting in mid-
2016 with an estimated cost of $6.8 million dollars. 
26. Professional Services (2016 – 2020) 
The Division issues RFPs every two (2) years for professional consultants to provide general engineering 
services to WPC. These services include wastewater system design and planning, sewer system design, 
regulatory support, bidding and construction services, surveying, field representation and operations 
support. At times sewer system investigations would include sewer line cleaning and jetting and short 
circuit television inspections. Services related to stormwater systems are typically included such as 
NPDES permitting and MS4 compliance assistance, BMP evaluations, eco-restoration, stream modeling 
and public education services.  
27. Technology (2016 – 2020) 
WPC direct cost share from IT for WPC technology investment projects. 
28. Undesignated (2017 – 2020) 
Includes projects to address recommendations of the WPC’s five year SSES program and condition 
assessments.

APPENDIX C 
Significant Assumptions 
 
  
APPENDIX C 
SIGNIFICANT ASSUMPTIONS 
 
Summary of Significant Forecast Assumptions and Notes to WPC Financial Forecast 
The accompanying Forecast, consisting of Table 8-6, “Cash Flow Projection (FY2016 through FY2020)”, 
presents WPC’s calculations of the Debt Service Coverage Ratio Requirement and the financial results of 
operations on a cash basis for FY2016 and the subsequent four fiscal years ending December 31, 2020 
(collectively referred to as the Forecast Period). It should be noted that projected revenues and expenses 
for FY2016 were based on amounts included in WPC’s Proposed Operating Budget for FY2016, dated 
January 8, 2016.   
This summary of significant assumptions provides information regarding the basis of the Forecast and 
support for the underlying assumptions. Arcadis has reviewed these underlying assumptions for purposes 
of providing an opinion and making certain conclusions regarding the reasonableness of the Forecast, as 
shown in Section 8 of this Report. The Forecast has been prepared based on assumptions concerning 
future events and circumstances and WPC’s most likely courses of action and best estimate of the 
financial results of operations during the Forecast Period. 
Significant Assumptions WPC: 
Customer Information: 
1. Number of Customer Meter Accounts 
Number of metered customer accounts used by WPC to calculate fixed fee revenues.  Meters vary 
from ½-inch to 12-inch diameter and includes homestead customers. For the purposes of these 
projections, the net number of customer metered accounts was projected to remain flat over the 
Forecast Period.  
2. Consumption User Charge 
This is the regular volumetric charge of per MCF of billable metered water consumption. The 
volumetric user charges have been approved by City Council through FY2019. The FY2020 charge i s 
a projected based on the proposed financial plan, and is subject to Board of Control and City Council 
approval. The WPC offers certain qualifying customers a discounted (60% off regular rate) 
“homestead” rate to qualifying customers. The homestead rate customers represent a very small 
number, approximately three percent (3%) of the annual revenues. 
Billing Revenues: 
3. Consumption User Charge Revenues 
Based on the FY2016 adopted budget and projected over the forecast period.  These revenues were 
based on a 2.2 percent decline in billable metered water consumption and required rate revenue 
increases beginning in FY2020, subject to Board of Control recommendation and City Council 
authorization. Also assumes that billing collection rates will remain consistent with historic averages, 
which have averaged approximately ninety percent (90%) per year. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx C-1  
4. Fixed Charge Revenue 
Beginning in FY2015, WPC charged customers a fixed fee based on meter size.  WPC’s authorized 
rates and projections were used for FY2016 through FY2019, which includes a rate increase in 
FY2017 and FY2019. A fixed charge rate increase is also projected for FY2020, subject to Board of 
Control recommendation and City Council authorization. 
5. Rate Revenue from Increase 
Required rate revenue increases from WPC’s adopted schedule for FY2016 – FY2019 and as 
projected by the financial plan beginning in FY2020. FY2020 rate increases subject to Board of 
Control and City Council authorization. 
6. Miscellaneous Revenue 
Includes revenue from City Division & Cost Plus Jobs, Licenses & Permits, Interest Income, and any 
other offsets.  These revenues were projected to be constant to match projections from WPC.  
7. Total Revenues 
Sum of Line Items 4, 5 and 6. 
Operating Expenses 
8. through 15.  
Operating and maintenance expenses were grouped as personnel expenses, other training and 
professional services, utilities, contractual services, materials and supplies, maintenance, claims, 
interdepartmental charges, and minor capital expenses.  These costs were based on WPC’s Adopted 
Budget for FY2016.  Future costs were projected using an escalation rate associated with each 
specific group. Escalation rates for the various expense groups was based on discussions with WPC 
regarding system operational changes, historical cost trends, and anticipated future wastewater flows 
and billed consumption trends. 
16. Total Operating Expense 
Sum of Line Items 8 through 15. 
17. Net Revenues Available for Debt Service 
Line Item 16 Total Operating Expenses, less Line Item 7 Total Revenues. 
18. Existing Debt Service 
Consists of the following debt service schedule: OPWC Loan - Kerruish Storm Water Management 
Facility, OPWC Loan - Hamlet Ave. & Adolpha Road Area Storm Sewer, OWDA Loan - Sewer 
Construction, OWDA Loan - Spring Road Sewers, OWDA Loan - Ivermere Avenue Vacinity Sewers, 
and OWDA Loan - Cooley Avenue Replacement Sewers. 
19. Series 2016 Revenue Bonds 
A debt service schedule was provided by the City’s financial advisors and is based on final pricing 
dated March 31, 2016. Proceeds are used to fund $35 million of project disbursements, a fully funded 
debt service reserve fund, and costs of issuance. 
arcadis.com 
z:\wp\bond feasibility report\final cleveland bond report march 31_2016ff.docx C-2  
20. New Debt Service for Capital Improvements 
New Debt Service represents anticipated debt service payments required to fund planned capital 
project costs not funded by cash or remaining proceeds from the 2016 Revenue Bonds. New revenue 
bonds were assumed to be issued over a term of thirty (30) years at an interest rate of five percent 
(5%) per year. Proceeds are used to fund approximately $16.1 million of project disbursements, a 
fully funded debt service reserve fund and costs of issuance. 
21. Total Debt Service 
Sum of Line Items 18, 19, and 20. 
Debt Service Coverage: 
22. DSC (Revenue Bond Debt, 120% minimum) 
Calculated by dividing Net Revenues Available for Debt Service Coverage (Line Item 17) by the Total 
Revenue Bond Debt (Sum of Line Items 19 and 20).  
23. DSC (All Debt) 
Calculated by dividing the Net Revenues Available for Debt Service Coverage (Line Item 17) by the 
Total Debt Service (Line Item 21).  
24  Minor Capital Expense 
Includes minor capital expenses such as computer hardware which are excluded from Net Revenues 
for purposes of calculating Debt Service Coverage.  
25  Net Revenues before Cash Funding of CIP 
Total Revenues (Line Item 7) less the sum of the Total Operating Expenses (Line Item 16), Total 
Debt Service (Line Item 21) and Minor Capital Expense (Line Item 24).  
WPC Cash Fund Balance Summary: 
26. Beginning Balance 
The beginning cash balance of the enterprise fund was based on the ending unrestricted cash 
balance within the fund based on WPC’s FY2015 unaudited financial statements.   
27. Net Revenues before Cash Funding of CIP 
Equal to Line Item 25. 
28 Transfers to Capital Projects Fund 
Transfer to Capital Projects Fund in an amount pursuant to the propose Capital Plan to cash fund 
certain capital improvements. 
29. Ending Balance 
Sum of Items 26, 27 and 28. 
30. Minimum Operating Reserve (6 Months)

 G-1 
APPENDIX G  
BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM 
The Depository Trust Company (“DTC”), New York, NY , will act as securities depository 
for the securities (the “Series 2016 Bonds”).  The Series 2016 Bonds will be issued as fully-
registered securities registered in the name of Cede & Co. (DTC’s partnership nominee) or such 
other name as may be requested by an authoriz ed representative of DTC.  One fully-registered 
Bond certificate will be issued for each stated ma turity of the Series 2016 Bonds, each in the 
aggregate principal amount of such issue, and will be deposited with DTC. So long as Cede & 
Co. is the registered owner of the Series 2016 Bonds, as partnership nominee for DTC, 
references herein to Bondholders, holders or ow ners of the Series 2016 Bonds (other than 
under the captions “Tax Matters” and “Continuing Disclosure Agreement” herein) shall 
mean Cede & Co. and shall not mean the Beneficial Owners of the Series 2016 Bonds. 
DTC, the world’s largest securities depos itory, is a limited-purpose trust company 
organized under the New York Banking Law, a “banking organization” within the meaning of the 
New York Banking Law, a member of the Federa l Reserve System, a “clearing corporation” 
within the meaning of the New York Unifor m Commercial Code, and a “clearing agency” 
registered pursuant to the provisions of Sectio n 17A of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934.  
DTC holds and provides asset servicing for over 3.5 million issues of U.S. and non-U.S. equity 
issues, corporate and municipa l debt issues, and money mark et instruments (from over 100 
countries) that DTC’s participants (“Direct Participants”) deposit w ith DTC.  DTC also 
facilitates the post-trade settlement among Direct  Participants of sale s and other securities 
transactions in deposited securities, through electronic computerized book-entry transfers and 
pledges between Direct Participants’ accounts.  Th is eliminates the need for physical movement 
of securities certificates.  Direct Participants  include both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers 
and dealers, banks, trust companies, clearing corporations, and certain other organizations.  DTC 
is a wholly-owned subsidiary of The Deposit ory Trust & Clearing Corporation (“DTCC”).  
DTCC is the holding company for DTC, National Securities Clearing Corporation and Fixed 
Income Clearing Corporation, all of which are re gistered clearing agencies.  DTCC is owned by 
the users of its regulated subsidiaries.  Access to the DTC system is also available to others such 
as both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers and dealers, banks, trust companies, and clearing 
corporations that clear through or maintain a cu stodial relationship with a Direct Participant, 
either directly or indirectly (“Indirect Partic ipants”).  DTC has a Standard & Poor’s rating of 
AA+.  The DTC Rules applicable to its Participan ts are on file with the Securities and Exchange 
Commission.  More information about DTC can be found at www.dtcc.com.  
Purchases of Series 2016 Bonds under the DT C system must be made by or through 
Direct Participants, which will receive a credit for the Series 2016 Bonds on DTC’s records.  The 
ownership interest of each actual purchaser of each Security (“Beneficial Owner”) is in turn to be 
recorded on the Direct and Indirect Participants ’ records.  Beneficial Owners will not receive 
written confirmation from DTC of their purchase.  Beneficial Owners are, however, expected to 
receive written confirmations providing details of the transaction, as  well as periodic statements 
of their holdings, from the Direct or Indirect  Participant through which the Beneficial Owner 
entered into the transaction.  Transfers of ownership interests in the Series 2016 Bonds are to be 
accomplished by entries made on the books of Direct  and Indirect Participants acting on behalf  
G-2 
of Beneficial Owners.  Beneficial Owners w ill not receive certificates representing their 
ownership interests in Series 2016 Bonds, except in the event th at use of the book-entry system 
for the Series 2016 Bonds is discontinued.   
To facilitate subsequent transfers, all Series 2016 Bonds deposited by Direct Participants 
with DTC are registered in the name of DTC’s partnership nominee, Cede & Co., or such other 
name as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC.  The deposit of Series 2016 
Bonds with DTC and their regist ration in the name of Cede & Co. or such other DTC nominee 
do not effect any change in beneficial ow nership.  DTC has no knowledge of the actual 
Beneficial Owners of the Series 2016 Bonds.  DT C’s records reflect only the identity of the 
Direct Participants to whose accounts such Series 2016 Bonds are cred ited, which may or may 
not be the Beneficial Owners.  The Direct and Indirect Particip ants will remain responsible for 
keeping account of their holdings on behalf of their customers.  
Conveyance of notices and ot her communications by DTC to Direct Participants, by 
Direct Participants to Indirect Participants, and by Direct Participants and Indirect Participants to 
Beneficial Owners will be governed by arrangemen ts among them, subject to any statutory or 
regulatory requirements as may be in effect from time to time.  Beneficial Owners of the Series 
2016 Bonds may wish to take certain  steps to augment the transmi ssion to them of notices of 
significant events with respect to  the Series 2016 Bonds, such as  redemptions, tenders, defaults, 
and proposed amendments to the offering documents. For example, Beneficial Owners of the 
Series 2016 Bonds may wish to  ascertain that the nominee hol ding the Series 2016 Bonds for 
their benefit has agreed to obtain and transmit notic es to Beneficial Owners. In the alternative, 
Beneficial Owners may wish to provide their names and addresse s to the registrar and request 
that copies of notices be provided directly to them. 
Redemption notices shall be sent to DTC.  If less than all of a series of the Series 2016 
Bonds within an issue are being redeemed, DTC' s practice is to determine by lot the amount of 
the interest of each Direct Participant in such issue to be redeemed.   
Neither DTC nor Cede & Co. (nor any othe r DTC nominee) will co nsent or vote with 
respect to Series 2016 Bonds unless authorized by a Direct Participant in accordance with DTC’s 
MMI Procedures.  Under its usual procedures, DTC mails an Omnibus Proxy to the City as soon 
as possible after the record date.  The Omnibus Proxy assigns Cede & Co.’s consenting or voting 
rights to those Direct Partic ipants to whose accounts Series 2016 Bonds are credited on the 
record date (identified in a listing attached to the Omnibus Proxy).  
Redemption proceeds, distributions, and dividend payments on the Series 2016 Bonds 
will be made to Cede & Co., or such other no minee as may be requested by an authorized 
representative of DTC.  DTC’ s practice is to credit Direct  Participants’ accounts upon DTC’s 
receipt of funds and corr esponding detail information from th e City or the Trustee, on payable 
date in accordance with their respective holdi ngs shown on DTC’s records.  Payments by 
Participants to Beneficial Owners will be gov erned by standing instructions and customary 
practices, as is the case with securities held fo r the accounts of customers in bearer form or 
registered in “street name,” and will be the responsibility of such Participant and not of DTC, the 
Trustee, or the City, subject to any statutory or regulatory requirements as may be in effect from 
time to time.  Payment of redemption proceeds, distributions, and dividend payments to Cede &  
G-3 
Co. (or such other nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC) is the 
responsibility of the Trustee, disbursement of su ch payments to Direct Participants will be the 
responsibility of DTC, and disbursement of such  payments to the Beneficial Owners will be the 
responsibility of Direct and Indirect Participants.  
A Beneficial Owner shall give notice to elec t to have its Series 2016 Bonds purchased or 
tendered, through its Participant, to the Paying Agen t, and shall effect delivery of such Series 
2016 Bonds by causing the Direct Partic ipant to transfer the Particip ant’s interest in the Series 
2016 Bonds, on DTC’s records, to the Paying Agent.   The requirement for physical delivery of 
Series 2016 Bonds in connection with an opt ional tender or a mandatory purchase will be 
deemed satisfied when the ownership rights in the Series 2016 Bonds are transferred by Direct 
Participants on DTC’s records and followed by a book-entry credit of tendered Series 2016 
Bonds to the Paying Agent’s DTC account.  
DTC may discontinue providing its services as depository with respect to the Series 2016 
Bonds at any time by gi ving reasonable notice to the City  or the Trustee.  Under such 
circumstances, in the event that a successor de pository is not obtained, Bond certificates are 
required to be printed and delivered.  
The City may decide to discontinue use of the system of book entry only transfers 
through DTC (or a successor securities depository) .  In that event, B ond certificates will be 
printed and delivered to DTC.  
The information in this section concerni ng DTC and DTC’s book-entry system has been 
obtained from sources that the City believes to be reliable, but the City takes no responsibility for 
the accuracy thereof.  
Direct Participants and Indirect Participants may impose service charges on book entry 
interest owners in certain cases.  Purchase rs of book entry interests should discuss that 
possibility with their brokers. 
The City and the Trustee have no role in th e purchases, transfers or sales of book entry 
interests.  The rights of Beneficial Owners (i.e., book-entry interest owners) to transfer or pledge 
their interests, and the manner of transferring or  pledging those interests, may be subject to 
applicable state law.  Beneficial Owners may want to discuss with their legal advisers the manner 
of transferring or pledging their book entry interests. 
The City and the Trustee have no responsibility or liability for any aspects of the records 
or notices relating to, or paym ents made on account of, book entr y interest ownership, or for 
maintaining, supervising or reviewing any records relating to that ownership. 
The City cannot and does not give any assurances  that DTC, Direct Participants, Indirect 
Participants or others will distribute to the Be neficial Owners payments of debt charges on the 
Series 2016 Bonds made to DTC as the registered owner, or any redemption or other notices, or 
that the City will do so on a timely basis, or that DTC will serve and act in a manner described in 
this Official Statement. [THIS PAGE INTENTIONALLY LEFT BLANK] CITY Of CLEvELaNd, OhIO • Water Pollution Control revenue Bonds, series 2016 (Green Bonds)
